# Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Introduction

Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [What do you want to build?](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#what-do-you-want-to-build)
    
*   [Quick Start with SDKs](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#quick-start-with-sdks)
    
*   [Additional Resources](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#additional-resources)
    
*   [Getting Help](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#getting-help)
    

Build blockchain analytics workflows with Dune’s comprehensive API suite. Access the same data that powers thousands of Dune dashboards, available programmatically for your data pattern needs. Dune API provides a variety of endpoints for **analysts**, **data engineers**, and **data scientists**, ranging from low-level, customizable options to connectors ready for immediate use. Queries saved in the Dune App UI can be executed via API and results retrieved in your environment, enabling bulk data extraction and automated workflows.

**New to Dune?** **[Create a free account](https://dune.com/auth/register)
** or **[get your API key](https://dune.com/apis?tab=keys)
** to get started.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#what-do-you-want-to-build)

What do you want to build?
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Analyze onchain data programmatically\
-------------------------------------\
\
Execute SQL queries, retrieve results, and build custom analytics pipelines with Dune’s query execution engine. Perfect for data teams and analysts.→ Start with query execution](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/apis/quickstart-analyze)
[Run queries in your environment\
-------------------------------\
\
Connect directly to Dune’s data warehouse using Trino Connector for maximum flexibility. Perfect for enterprise teams with existing BI tools.→ Set up Trino connector](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/overview)
[Build custom dashboards & reports\
---------------------------------\
\
Fetch query results, manage executions, and create dynamic visualizations in your own applications. Perfect for teams embedding analytics.→ Create your first dashboard](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/apis/quickstart-dashboards)
[Build real-time applications\
----------------------------\
\
Create a multichain wallet with realtime balances, transactions, and NFTs using Sim by Dune. Perfect for mobile developers and DeFi applications.→ Build a realtime wallet with Sim](https://docs.sim.dune.com/evm/build-a-realtime-wallet)
[Transform data with dbt\
-----------------------\
\
Build production-grade data transformation pipelines with write access to DuneSQL. Perfect for data engineering teams using dbt.→ Set up dbt connector](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview)
[BI Visualization Tools\
----------------------\
\
Connect Dune to your favorite BI tools like Hex, Metabase, and DBeaver using the Trino/Presto connector.→ Connect BI tools](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview)

[Get started with the basics\
---------------------------\
\
New to APIs? Start here to make your first request and see results in minutes.Learn how to execute a simple SQL query, authenticate your requests, and retrieve blockchain data programmatically.→ Make your first request](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/getting-started)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#quick-start-with-sdks)

Quick Start with SDKs
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Our SDKs handle authentication, polling, pagination, and error handling automatically. The new `execute()` function manages the entire workflow for you.

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#python)

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#python)

[Python\
------](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#python)

[Copy\
\
Ask AI\
\
    pip install dune-client\
    \
\
Copy\
\
Ask AI\
\
    from dune_client import DuneClient\
    \
    dune = DuneClient(api_key="your-key")\
    results = dune.execute(query_id=3493826)](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#python)

[Full Python documentation →](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#python)

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#typescript)

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#typescript)

[TypeScript\
----------](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#typescript)

[Copy\
\
Ask AI\
\
    npm install @duneanalytics/client\
    \
\
Copy\
\
Ask AI\
\
    import { DuneClient } from '@duneanalytics/client';\
    \
    const dune = new DuneClient('your-key');\
    const results = await dune.execute({ queryId: 3493826 });](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#typescript)

[Full TypeScript documentation →](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#typescript)

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#go)

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#go)

[Go\
--](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#go)

[Copy\
\
Ask AI\
\
    go get github.com/duneanalytics/duneapi-client-go\
    \
\
Copy\
\
Ask AI\
\
    client := duneapi.New("your-key")\
    results := client.Execute(3493826)](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#go)

[Full Go documentation →](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/sdks#go)

**New:** All SDKs now include an `execute()` function that handles polling and pagination automatically. No more managing multiple API calls!

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction#additional-resources)

# Dune CLI & Skills - Dune Docs

Agents

Dune CLI & Skills

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)

On this page

*   [Dune CLI](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#dune-cli)
    
*   [Install](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#install)
    
*   [Authenticate (manual)](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#authenticate-manual)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#usage)
    
*   [Dune Skills](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#dune-skills)
    
*   [Install](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#install-2)
    
*   [How it works](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#how-it-works)
    
*   [Key Benefits](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#key-benefits)
    
*   [Use Cases](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#use-cases)
    

The Dune CLI and Agent Skills give your AI coding agent structured access to Dune’s datasets, query engine, and documentation — directly inside the tools you already use. The **Dune CLI** is a terminal-native interface for discovering datasets, executing DuneSQL queries, and managing results. **Dune Skills** are portable instruction packages that teach AI agents how to use the CLI effectively — from writing correct SQL to handling errors and optimizing costs. Together, they turn any skills-compatible agent into a blockchain data analyst.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#dune-cli)

Dune CLI
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Dune CLI lets you query, explore, and manage blockchain data without leaving your terminal. All commands support both human-readable and JSON output, making them equally useful for interactive work and agent-driven workflows.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#install)

Install

Copy

Ask AI

    curl -sSfL https://dune.com/cli/install.sh | sh
    

The install script handles everything you need to get started: it installs the Dune CLI, runs `dune auth` to configure your API key, and installs the Dune Agent Skill via `npx skills add`. In most cases, this single command is all you need.

You’ll need a Dune API key during setup. Generate one at [dune.com](https://dune.com/)
 under **APIs and Connectors > API Keys** before running the install script.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#authenticate-manual)

Authenticate (manual)

If you need to re-authenticate or configure a different API key after installation, you can run:

Copy

Ask AI

    dune auth
    

You’ll be prompted to enter your API key. It’s saved to `~/.config/dune/config.yaml` for future sessions. Alternatively, pass the key inline or via environment variable:

Copy

Ask AI

    # Environment variable
    export DUNE_API_KEY=<your-api-key>
    
    # Inline flag
    dune query run 12345 --api-key <your-api-key>
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#usage)

Usage

Run `dune --help` to see all available commands. All commands support `-o json` for structured, machine-parseable output — ideal for agent consumption:

Copy

Ask AI

    dune query run-sql --sql "SELECT * FROM ethereum.transactions LIMIT 5" -o json
    

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#dune-skills)

Dune Skills
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Agent Skills](https://agentskills.io/)
 are an open standard for giving AI agents new capabilities. The Dune Skill teaches your agent how to use the Dune CLI to discover datasets, write DuneSQL, execute queries, handle errors, and manage costs — all from natural language prompts. Skills are supported by Claude Code, Cursor, OpenCode, OpenAI Codex, VS Code, Gemini CLI, Goose, and [many more](https://agentskills.io/)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#install-2)

Install

The Dune Skill is automatically installed when you run the [CLI install script](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#install)
 above — no extra steps required. If you need to install or reinstall the skill separately, you can run:

Copy

Ask AI

    npx skills add duneanalytics/skills
    

*   Claude Code
    
*   Cursor
    
*   Manual
    

Skills are automatically installed to `~/.claude/skills/` and loaded when your conversation matches blockchain-related triggers.

You can also add the skill via **Settings > Rules > Add Rule > Remote Rule (Github)** with `duneanalytics/skills`.

Clone the [duneanalytics/skills](https://github.com/duneanalytics/skills)
 repository and copy the `skills/dune/` folder into your agent’s skill directory:

| Agent | Directory |
| --- | --- |
| Claude Code | `~/.claude/skills/` |
| Cursor | `~/.cursor/skills/` |
| OpenCode | `~/.config/opencode/skills/` |
| OpenAI Codex | `~/.codex/skills/` |

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#how-it-works)

How it works

Once installed, the Dune Skill activates automatically when your conversation involves blockchain data, on-chain analytics, DuneSQL, token transfers, DEX trades, smart contract events, or wallet analysis. The agent then:

1.  Discovers the right tables using `dune dataset search`
2.  Inspects column schemas to build correct SQL
3.  Writes DuneSQL with proper partition filters for cost efficiency
4.  Executes the query and parses results
5.  Handles errors with built-in recovery strategies

The skill includes detailed reference documents for query execution, dataset discovery, DuneSQL syntax, and error handling — loaded on demand to keep context window usage efficient.

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#key-benefits)

Key Benefits
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Agent-Native Data Access
------------------------

Your AI agent queries blockchain data directly — no context switching, no copy-pasting SQL between apps.

Works Where You Work
--------------------

Compatible with Claude Code, Cursor, VS Code, Codex, and any agent that supports the Agent Skills standard.

Cost-Aware by Default
---------------------

The skill teaches agents to filter on partition columns and choose the right performance tier, reducing credit consumption.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills#use-cases)

Use Cases
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Ad-Hoc Analysis
---------------

Ask your agent a question in plain English and get results backed by DuneSQL — from DEX volumes to gas trends.

Contract Exploration
--------------------

Give the agent a contract address and let it discover all decoded event and call tables automatically.

Pipeline Scripting
------------------

Use the CLI’s JSON output and async execution to integrate Dune queries into CI/CD pipelines or monitoring scripts.

Reusable Parameterized Queries
------------------------------

Create saved queries with parameters, then run them with different inputs across sessions.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Overview](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object)

*   [Getting Started](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#getting-started)
    

Data Transformations is an **Enterprise-only feature** with usage-based credit consumption.

**CI/CD and Credit Usage**Each dbt execution consumes credits, whether triggered locally, through CI/CD, or on a schedule. The template repository ships with automated CI/CD triggers **disabled by default** so you can enable them when you’re ready. See [CI/CD & Workflows](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows)
 for tips on managing costs in automated pipelines.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#pricing-&-credits)

Pricing & Credits
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#credit-consumption)

Credit Consumption

Your credit usage includes three components:

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#compute-credits)

Compute Credits

*   Same as Fluid Engine credits for query execution
*   Charged based on actual compute resources used
*   Depends on query complexity and execution time

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#write-operations)

Write Operations

*   **Minimum 3 credits** per write operation
*   Scales with data volume (GB written)
*   Applied to INSERT, MERGE, CREATE TABLE AS SELECT, etc.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#storage-credits)

Storage Credits

*   **4 credits per GB per month**
*   Calculated based on end-of-day storage usage
*   Encourages efficient data management and cleanup

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#maintenance-operations)

Maintenance Operations

*   OPTIMIZE, VACUUM, and ANALYZE operations consume credits
*   Based on compute resources and data written during maintenance
*   Can be automated with dbt post-hooks

There is no separate platform fee. You only pay for what you use through credits. See [Billing](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/billing)
 for more details on credit pricing.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#best-practices)

Best Practices
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#model-organization)

Model Organization

Copy

Ask AI

    models/
    ├── staging/           # Clean and standardize raw data
    ├── intermediate/      # Business logic transformations  
    ├── marts/            # Final datasets for analytics
    └── utils/            # Reusable utility models
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#schema-organization)

Schema Organization

*   Use `dev` target with personal suffixes during development
*   Keep `prod` target for production deployments only
*   Consider separate schemas for different projects or domains

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#performance-optimization)

Performance Optimization

*   Use incremental models for large datasets
*   Partition by date fields when possible
*   Add appropriate partitions via dbt configurations
*   Run OPTIMIZE and VACUUM on large tables

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#credit-management)

Credit Management

*   Monitor credit usage in your Dune dashboard
*   Use incremental models to reduce compute and write costs
*   Drop unused development tables regularly
*   Implement table lifecycle policies

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#data-management)

Data Management

*   Clean up temporary/test data in `__tmp_` schemas
*   Document table retention requirements
*   Regularly review and optimize storage usage

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#version-control)

Version Control

*   Store all transformation logic in Git
*   Use meaningful commit messages
*   Tag production releases
*   Review PRs before merging to main

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#documentation)

Documentation

Copy

Ask AI

    # schema.yml
    models:
      - name: user_stats
        description: "Daily user trading statistics"
        columns:
          - name: user_address
            description: "Ethereum address of the user"
            tests:
              - not_null
              - unique
          - name: trade_count
            description: "Number of trades in the period"
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices#resources)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

BI Visualization Tools

Metabase

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)

On this page

*   [Add the Database Connection](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#add-the-database-connection)
    
*   [Run a Test Query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#run-a-test-query)
    

Follow these steps to connect Dune as a data source in Metabase.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#add-the-database-connection)

Add the Database Connection
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Open Admin settings

From the Metabase home page, click the **Settings** gear icon in the top-right corner. Select **Admin settings** from the dropdown menu.

![Metabase step 1: Open Admin settings](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY/images/trino-presto-connector/metabase-1.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY&q=85&s=11d62b503861c1281e4cb40a9be58f06)

2

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Go to Databases

In the Admin panel, navigate to the **Databases** tab.

![Metabase step 2: Go to Databases](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY/images/trino-presto-connector/metabase-2.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY&q=85&s=447561935cfe3b803c0c8acfa686d518)

3

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Add database

Click the blue **Add database** button to open the configuration modal.

![Metabase step 3: Add database](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY/images/trino-presto-connector/metabase-3.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY&q=85&s=65ba403f996e229014f1a01862b27c36)

4

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Choose driver

In the modal, select `Starburst (Trino)` as the **Database type**.

5

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Enter connection details

Fill in the form fields using the values from the [Connection Parameters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#connection-parameters)
 section. For best performance in Metabase, we recommend disabling **Rerun queries for simple explorations** and **Periodically refingerprint tables** in the advanced settings.

Schema discovery queries such as `SHOW TABLES` or `SHOW SCHEMAS` may not be available in Metabase with this connector because Dune’s catalog spans millions of tables. Many BI tools are not yet optimized to enumerate catalogs at this scale. An update with improved schema discovery is planned for the future.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#run-a-test-query)

Run a Test Query
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After configuring and saving the connection, you can run a query to verify that everything is working.

1

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Create a new SQL query

Click the **\+ New** button and select **SQL query**.

2

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Select database

In the editor, choose your newly created **Dune SQL** data source from the **Select a database** dropdown.

3

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Paste example SQL

Paste the example query below into the editor.

4

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase#)

Run the query

Run the query to verify the connection.

You can use this query to test your connection. It fetches the daily transaction count from the last year on Base.

Copy

Ask AI

    SELECT
      date_trunc('day', block_time) AS time,
      count(*) AS count
    FROM base.transactions
    WHERE block_time > now() - interval '12' month
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC

Run a Test Query
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once your data source is configured, you can query it directly from any Hex project.

1

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/hex#)

Open or create a project

Open an existing project or create a new one.

2

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/hex#)

Add a SQL cell

3

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/hex#)

Select data source

4

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/hex#)

Paste and run SQL

Paste the example query below into the cell and run it.

![Hex step: Paste and run SQL](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY/images/trino-presto-connector/hex-4.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY&q=85&s=54cd3f74347c6fd2168afeee30875ef7)

You can use this query to test your connection. It fetches the daily transaction count from the last year on Base.

Copy

Ask AI

    SELECT
      date_trunc('day', block_time) AS time,
      count(*) AS count
    FROM base.transactions
    WHERE block_time > now() - interval '12' month
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC

Follow these steps to connect Dune as a data source in DBeaver.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#add-a-database-connection)

Add a Database Connection
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Create new connection

In DBeaver, click the **New Database Connection** button. It usually looks like a plug with a plus on it.

2

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Select Trino database

You’ll be taken to the “Connect to a database” screen. Find and select **Trino** from the list of accepted databases, then click on it.

![DBeaver step 2: Select Trino from database list](https://mintcdn.com/dune/bE2iCQxUVMqVPGif/images/trino-presto-connector/dbeaver-1.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=bE2iCQxUVMqVPGif&q=85&s=aaf44d48889e342d96458e915df30599)

3

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Configure connection details

You’ll be taken to a screen where you can fill in your connection details. Make sure to click **Connect by host**, then fill in the connection parameters using the values from the [Connection Parameters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#connection-parameters)
 section.

![DBeaver step 3: Enter connection details](https://mintcdn.com/dune/bE2iCQxUVMqVPGif/images/trino-presto-connector/dbeaver-2.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=bE2iCQxUVMqVPGif&q=85&s=1dd1a1aa792441f2640e54f9eb6bad43)

4

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Finish connection setup

Once you have all the details filled out properly, click **Finish** to create the connection.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#run-a-test-query)

Run a Test Query
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After configuring your connection, you can run a query to verify that everything is working.

1

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Open SQL editor

Right-click on your Dune database connection and navigate to the **SQL Editor** section. This will open up a new SQL editor.

2

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Write your SQL query

In the SQL editor, you can write all of your Dune-compatible SQL. Paste the example query below into the editor.

3

[](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver#)

Run the script

Click the **Run** button to execute your script. If everything went well, you will see the results displayed in the results panel.

![DBeaver step 5: Run SQL script and view results](https://mintcdn.com/dune/bE2iCQxUVMqVPGif/images/trino-presto-connector/dbeaver-3.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=bE2iCQxUVMqVPGif&q=85&s=d3d55c612503e2091e0631ad507df9e6)

You can use this query to test your connection. It fetches the daily transaction count from the last year on Base.

Copy

Ask AI

    SELECT
      date_trunc('day', block_time) AS time,
      count(*) AS count
    FROM base.transactions
    WHERE block_time > now() - interval '12' month
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC

Transform your Data

dbt Connector Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)

*   [Why dbt on Dune?](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#why-dbt-on-dune)

*   [Next Steps](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#next-steps)
    
*   [SQLMesh Compatibility](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#sqlmesh-compatibility)
    

The dbt Connector enables you to run production-grade dbt projects directly against Dune’s data warehouse using the [dbt-trino adapter](https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/core/connect-data-platform/trino-setup)
. Build, test, and deploy transformation pipelines with full support for incremental models, testing frameworks, and CI/CD orchestration. This connector provides **write access to DuneSQL** via a Trino API endpoint, enabling you to create, update, and manage tables in your private namespace while reading from Dune’s comprehensive blockchain datasets.[dbt Template Repository\
-----------------------\
\
Get started quickly with our official dbt template repository, featuring example models for all model strategies and CI/CD workflows.](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template)

The dbt Connector is currently only available to Enterprise customers with Data Transformations enabled.

Interested in having the dbt Connector enabled for your team? [Contact our team](https://dune.com/enterprise)
—please mention the dbt Connector when you reach out.

**Credits & CI/CD**Each dbt run consumes Dune credits, including runs triggered by CI/CD pipelines. If you’re using GitHub Actions or similar tools, we recommend reviewing [Pricing & Best Practices](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices)
 for optimization tips and [CI/CD & Workflows](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows)
 for guidance on configuring triggers.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#video-tutorial)

Video Tutorial
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Watch this step-by-step guide to get started with the dbt Connector on Dune:

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#what-is-dbt)

What is dbt?
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[dbt (data build tool)](https://www.getdbt.com/)
 is the industry-standard framework for analytics engineering. It enables data teams to transform raw data into analysis-ready datasets using SQL and software engineering best practices. **Key capabilities:**

*   **SQL-based transformations**: Write SELECT statements, dbt handles the DDL/DML
*   **Incremental models**: Efficiently update large tables with merge, append, or delete+insert strategies
*   **Testing & documentation**: Built-in data quality tests and auto-generated documentation
*   **Version control**: Manage transformation logic in Git with code review workflows
*   **Dependency management**: Define relationships between models with automatic execution ordering

[dbt Documentation\
-----------------\
\
Learn more about dbt’s features, best practices, and advanced capabilities in the official dbt documentation.](https://docs.getdbt.com/)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#why-dbt-on-dune)

Why dbt on Dune?
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#enterprise-grade-transformations)

Enterprise-Grade Transformations

*   **Full incremental support**: Use merge, delete+insert, or append strategies for efficient updates
*   **Testing framework**: Validate data quality with dbt’s built-in testing capabilities
*   **Documentation**: Generate and maintain documentation alongside your transformations
*   **Modularity**: Build reusable models and macros for complex transformation logic

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#seamless-integration)

Seamless Integration

*   **Drop-in compatibility**: Works with your existing dbt projects and workflows
*   **Version control**: Manage transformation logic in Git with PR reviews
*   **Production orchestration**: Schedule with GitHub Actions, Airflow, Prefect, or dbt Cloud. See [Pricing & Best Practices](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices)
     for credit optimization tips
*   **Private by default**: Keep proprietary transformation logic within your organization

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#no-spellbook-dependency)

No Spellbook Dependency

*   **Autonomous deployment**: Deploy transformations on your schedule without community review
*   **Proprietary logic**: Keep sensitive business logic private
*   **Faster iteration**: Test and deploy changes immediately

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#connection-details)

Connection Details
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Connect to Dune using these parameters:

| Parameter | Value |
| --- | --- |
| **Host** | `trino.api.dune.com` |
| **Port** | `443` |
| **Protocol** | HTTPS |
| **Catalog** | `dune` (required) |
| **Authentication** | JWT (use your Dune API key) |
| **Session Property** | `transformations=true` (required for write operations) |

The session property `transformations=true` is **required** for all write operations. Without it, DDL and DML statements will be rejected.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#use-cases)

Use Cases
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#enterprise-data-pipelines)

Enterprise Data Pipelines

Add Dune to your existing data infrastructure without reworking your workflows:

*   **Drop-in compatibility**: Integrate with your current dbt projects, Airflow DAGs, or Prefect flows
*   **Full incremental support**: Use merge, delete+insert, or append strategies for efficient updates
*   **Production orchestration**: Schedule with the tools you already use (GitHub Actions, Airflow, Prefect)
*   **Version controlled**: Keep all transformation logic in Git alongside your other data pipelines

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#governance-&-compliance)

Governance & Compliance

Meet enterprise requirements for data control and auditability:

*   **Private by default**: All datasets remain private to your team unless explicitly shared
*   **Audit trails**: Track every transformation through Git history and PR workflows
*   **Data lineage**: Maintain clear lineage from raw data through transformations to analytics
*   **Review processes**: Implement PR reviews and approval workflows before deploying to production
*   **Access control**: Restrict write access to specific teams and namespaces

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#complex-analytics-workflows)

Complex Analytics Workflows

Build sophisticated multi-stage data pipelines:

*   Read from Dune’s comprehensive blockchain datasets across all chains
*   Transform and enrich with your proprietary business logic
*   Create reusable intermediate datasets for downstream analytics
*   Chain multiple transformations into complex data products

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#alternative-to-spellbook)

Alternative to Spellbook

Build and maintain custom datasets without community review processes:

*   Deploy transformations on your own schedule
*   Keep proprietary logic private to your organization
*   Faster iteration cycles without PR review delays

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#next-steps)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

\
Set up GitHub Actions and development workflows](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows)

Understand credit consumption and optimization tips](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview#sqlmesh-compatibility)

SQLMesh Compatibility
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[SQLMesh](https://sqlmesh.com/)
 also works out of the box with Dune using the same Trino connection approach described above. If you prefer SQLMesh over dbt for your data transformation workflows, you can connect it to Dune using the [SQLMesh Trino adapter](https://sqlmesh.readthedocs.io/en/stable/integrations/engines/trino/)
 with the same connection parameters.We plan to release a dedicated SQLMesh template in the future. Until then, follow the same connection setup (host, port, authentication, and session properties) to get started with SQLMesh on Dune.

# Trino Connector Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#content-area)

Trino Connector Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Compatible Tools](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#compatible-tools)
    
*   [Connection Parameters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#connection-parameters)
    
*   [Supported SQL Operations](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#supported-sql-operations)
    
*   [Rate Limits](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#rate-limits)

Access Dune’s blockchain data from your favorite BI tools and clients using the DuneSQL Trino/Presto connector. Connect Dune with popular tools like Hex, Metabase, DBeaver, and any Trino, Presto, or Starburst-compatible application for seamless data analysis.

![Dune Trino Presto connector architecture diagram showing integration flow](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY/images/trino-presto-connector/trino%20-%20light.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY&q=85&s=fbf8a40628116abb9567d03381f2a93f)![Dune Trino Presto connector architecture diagram showing integration flow](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY/images/trino-presto-connector/trino%20-%20dark.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Sfv_5QdqAPVofYTY&q=85&s=3a7f184dcde5a798fc1f4b864d77b848)

The DuneSQL Trino Connector is currently only available to Plus and Enterprise customers.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#compatible-tools)

Compatible Tools
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Dune’s Trino connector supports any tool that works with Trino, Presto, or Starburst connectors. Popular Dune integrations include:

[Hex\
---\
\
Connect Dune to Hex’s notebook-native analytics via built-in Trino connector.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/hex)
[Metabase\
--------\
\
Integrate Dune with Metabase using the Starburst/Trino driver for BI dashboards.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/metabase)
[DBeaver\
-------\
\
Connect Dune to DBeaver using the Trino driver for direct SQL access to blockchain data.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/dbeaver)
[Trino SDKs\
----------\
\
Treat Dune like a Database in your language of choice with popular Trino libraries.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/sdks)

Any of the supported client applications listed in the [Trino ecosystem](https://trino.io/ecosystem/#official-client-applications)
 are supported. Please visit their documentation to learn about their specific connection instructions, though the configuration should generally follow the same pattern using the connection parameters below.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#connection-parameters)

Connection Parameters
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use these values in your Trino, Presto, or Starburst client configuration:

| Parameter | Value | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Host | `trino.api.dune.com` | Dune’s Trino/Presto endpoint |
| Port | `443` | Standard HTTPS port |
| Username | `dune` | Fixed username for all connections |
| Password | `<your-dune-api-key>` | [Your Dune API key](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/authentication) |
| Catalog | `delta_prod` | Main data catalog |
| SSL/TLS | `true` | Always use encrypted connections |
| HTTP scheme | `https` | Required for secure connections |

If you need an API key, see our guide on [Authentication](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/authentication)
. Remember to keep your API keys secret and rotate them immediately if they are ever exposed.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#supported-sql-operations)

Supported SQL Operations
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Queries executed via the connector align with what you can run on the Dune platform. See the [Query Engine overview](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
 for more information on supported functions and syntax.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#rate-limits)

Rate Limits
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Rate limits for the connector mirror those of the Dune Data API. Please refer to the [Rate Limits](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/rate-limits)
 documentation for details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#billing-&-cost)

Billing & Cost
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All queries run via the connector are executed on the [Large Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#query-engine-size)
. Credits are consumed based on actual compute resources used. In addition, fetching results consumes credits proportional to the number of datapoints returned. For a full breakdown, please see our documentation on [Billing](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/billing)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#limitations)

Limitations
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The connector currently has limited support for metadata discovery queries such as `SHOW TABLES` or `SHOW SCHEMAS`. This may impact the data source browsing and autocomplete experience within some BI tools. For schema and table discovery, see the [Data Explorer](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/data-explorer)
 guide. If you encounter timeouts with large result sets, consider paginating your queries using `LIMIT` and `OFFSET`, narrowing your filters, or splitting complex queries into smaller, more manageable parts.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Supported SQL Operations](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/sql-operations)
[Hex](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/hex)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

The dbt template includes pre-configured GitHub Actions workflows for both CI and production deployments.

**Credit Usage in CI/CD**All dbt executions triggered by CI/CD workflows consume Dune credits. This includes pull request workflows, deploy workflows, and scheduled runs. The template repository ships with automated triggers **disabled by default** so you can enable them on your own terms. See [Pricing & Best Practices](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices)
 for optimization guidance.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#understanding-credit-costs-in-ci/cd)

Understanding Credit Costs in CI/CD
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When you run dbt models through CI/CD, each execution consumes credits from your Dune plan. Here are a few things to keep in mind:

*   **Each push or PR can trigger a pipeline run.** If your GitHub Actions run on every commit, frequent pushes during development will each use credits.
*   **All executions draw from the same pool.** Whether a query is triggered locally, from a CI runner, or a scheduled job, it counts the same way.
*   **Concurrent executions add up.** Multiple CI jobs running simultaneously (e.g., several open PRs) each consume credits independently.
*   **Timed-out queries still use credits.** If a query runs for 30 minutes before timing out, credits are consumed for the compute used during that time.

**Tips for managing costs:**

*   Start with `workflow_dispatch` (manual trigger only) until you’ve validated your models
*   Use `--select state:modified` to only run changed models in CI
*   Set appropriate query timeouts to keep costs predictable
*   Monitor your credit usage in the Dune dashboard after enabling automated workflows

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#development-workflow)

Development Workflow
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#local-development)

Local Development

1.  **Create a feature branch**:
    
    Copy
    
    Ask AI
    
        git checkout -b feature/new-transformation
        
    
2.  **Develop models locally**:
    
    Copy
    
    Ask AI
    
        # Run specific model
        uv run dbt run --select my_model
        
        # Run with full refresh (ignore incremental logic)
        uv run dbt run --select my_model --full-refresh
        
        # Run tests for specific model
        uv run dbt test --select my_model
        
    
3.  **Query your tables on Dune**:
    
    *   Remember to use the `dune.` catalog prefix:
    
    Copy
    
    Ask AI
    
        SELECT * FROM dune.my_team__tmp_alice.my_model
        
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#pull-request-workflow)

Pull Request Workflow

1.  **Push changes and open PR**:
    
    Copy
    
    Ask AI
    
        git add .
        git commit -m "Add new transformation model"
        git push origin feature/new-transformation
        
    
2.  **Automated CI runs**:
    *   CI enforces that branch is up-to-date with main
    *   Runs modified models with `--full-refresh` in isolated schema `{team}__tmp_pr{number}`
    *   Runs tests on modified models
    *   Tests incremental run logic

**Tip:** The pull request workflow is disabled by default in the template. To enable it, uncomment the `on:` trigger block in `.github/workflows/dbt_ci.yml`. Each PR sync event (new commits pushed to a PR branch) will trigger a run and consume credits.

3.  **Team review**:
    *   Review transformation logic in GitHub
    *   Check CI results
    *   Approve and merge when ready

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#production-deployment)

Production Deployment

The [production workflow](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template/blob/main/.github/workflows/dbt_prod.yml)
 includes an hourly schedule (0 \* \* \* \*), but it’s commented out by default. You can enable it by uncommenting the corresponding lines when you’re ready to run production jobs automatically.

**Tip:** The deploy and scheduled workflows are disabled by default. Only `workflow_dispatch` (manual trigger) is enabled out of the box. Uncomment the `push` and `schedule` triggers in the respective workflow files when you’re ready to automate.

1.  **State comparison**: Uses manifest from previous run to detect changes
2.  **Full refresh modified models**: Any changed models run with `--full-refresh`
3.  **Incremental run**: All models run with normal incremental logic
4.  **Testing**: All models are tested
5.  **Notification**: Email sent on failure

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#ci/cd-with-github-actions)

CI/CD with GitHub Actions
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The template includes two GitHub Actions workflows:

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#ci-workflow-github/workflows/ci-yml)

CI Workflow (`.github/workflows/ci.yml`)

Runs on every pull request:

Copy

Ask AI

    - Enforces branch is up-to-date with main
    - Sets DEV_SCHEMA_SUFFIX to pr{number}
    - Runs modified models with --full-refresh
    - Tests modified models
    - Runs incremental logic test
    - Tests incremental models
    

**Required GitHub Secrets**:

*   `DUNE_API_KEY`

**Required GitHub Variables**:

*   `DUNE_TEAM_NAME`

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#production-workflow-github/workflows/prod-yml)

Production Workflow (`.github/workflows/prod.yml`)

Runs hourly on main branch:

Copy

Ask AI

    - Downloads previous manifest (for state comparison)
    - Full refreshes any modified models
    - Tests modified models
    - Runs all models (incremental logic)
    - Tests all models
    - Uploads manifest for next run
    - Sends email notification on failure
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#connection-issues)

Connection Issues

**Problem**: `dbt debug` fails with connection error. **Solution**:

*   Verify `DUNE_API_KEY` and `DUNE_TEAM_NAME` are set correctly
*   Check that you have Data Transformations enabled for your team
*   Ensure `transformations: true` is in session properties

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#models-not-appearing-in-dune)

Models Not Appearing in Dune

**Problem**: Can’t find tables in Data Explorer or queries. **Solution**:

*   Check the Connectors section in Data Explorer under “My Data”
*   Remember to use `dune.` catalog prefix in queries
*   Verify the table was created in the correct schema

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#incremental-models-not-working)

Incremental Models Not Working

**Problem**: Incremental models always do full refresh. **Solution**:

*   Check that `is_incremental()` macro is used correctly
*   Verify the `unique_key` configuration matches your table structure
*   Ensure the target table exists before running incrementally

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#ci/cd-failures)

CI/CD Failures

**Problem**: GitHub Actions failing. **Solution**:

*   Verify secrets and variables are set correctly in GitHub
*   Check that branch is up-to-date with main
*   Review workflow logs for specific errors

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#limitations)

Limitations
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#metadata-discovery)

Metadata Discovery

Limited support for some metadata discovery queries like `SHOW TABLES` or `SHOW SCHEMAS` in certain contexts. This may affect autocomplete in some BI tools. **Workaround**: Use the [Data Explorer](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/data-explorer)
 or query `information_schema` directly.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#result-set-size)

Result Set Size

Large result sets may timeout. Consider:

*   Paginating with `LIMIT` and `OFFSET`
*   Narrowing filters to reduce data volume
*   Breaking complex queries into smaller parts

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#read-after-write-consistency)

Read-After-Write Consistency

Tables and views are available for querying immediately after creation, but catalog caching may cause brief delays (typically < 60 seconds) before appearing in some listing operations.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows#rate-limits)

Rate Limits

Rate limits for Data Transformations align with the Dune Data API:

*   Requests are subject to the same rate limiting as API executions
*   Large query operations run on the [Large Query Engine tier](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#large-engine-size)
    
*   See [Rate Limits](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/rate-limits)
     for detailed information

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Incremental Models](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models)
[Pricing & Best Practices](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices)

The fastest way to get started is using our [dbt template repository](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template)
, which includes pre-configured profiles, sample models, and CI/CD workflows.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#prerequisites)

Prerequisites
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Dune Enterprise account** with Data Transformations enabled
*   **Dune API key** ([generate one here](https://dune.com/settings/api)
    )
*   **Team name** on Dune (defines your namespace)
*   **dbt installed locally** (we recommend using `uv` for dependency management)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#1-use-the-template-repository)

1\. Use the Template Repository
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

We provide a complete dbt project template to get started quickly: **GitHub Template**: [github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template)
 The template includes:

*   Pre-configured dbt profiles for dev and prod environments
*   Sample models demonstrating all model types
*   GitHub Actions workflows for CI/CD
*   Cursor AI rules for dbt best practices on Dune
*   Example project structure following dbt conventions

**CI Workflows Are Disabled by Default**The template repository ships with GitHub Actions CI workflows **disabled by default**. Since each dbt execution consumes Dune credits, we recommend:

1.  Running models locally first to get familiar with your pipeline
2.  Reviewing the [Pricing & Best Practices](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/pricing-best-practices)
     guide
3.  Enabling workflows when you’re ready by uncommenting triggers in the workflow files (see the [template README](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template#-note-)
     for instructions)

**To use the template:**

Copy

Ask AI

    # Create a new repository from the template
    # (Use GitHub's "Use this template" button)
    
    # Clone your new repository
    git clone https://github.com/your-org/your-dbt-project.git
    cd your-dbt-project
    
    # Install dependencies
    uv sync
    
    # Set up environment variables (see next section)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#2-configure-environment-variables)

2\. Configure Environment Variables
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Set these required environment variables:

Copy

Ask AI

    # Required
    export DUNE_API_KEY="your_api_key_here"
    export DUNE_TEAM_NAME="your_team_name"
    
    # Optional - for personal dev environments
    export DEV_SCHEMA_SUFFIX="alice"
    

**Persistence options:**

Copy

Ask AI

    # Option 1: Add to shell profile (recommended for local dev)
    echo 'export DUNE_API_KEY="your_key"' >> ~/.zshrc
    echo 'export DUNE_TEAM_NAME="your_team"' >> ~/.zshrc
    source ~/.zshrc
    
    # Option 2: Use a .env file (remember to add to .gitignore!)
    # Option 3: Set in CI/CD secrets for production deployments
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#3-configure-dbt-profile)

3\. Configure dbt Profile
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Your `profiles.yml` should look like this:

Copy

Ask AI

    dune:
      outputs:
        dev:
          type: trino
          method: jwt
          user: "{{ env_var('DUNE_TEAM_NAME') }}"
          jwt_token: "{{ env_var('DUNE_API_KEY') }}"
          host: trino.api.dune.com
          port: 443
          database: dune
          schema: "{{ env_var('DUNE_TEAM_NAME') }}__tmp_{{ env_var('DEV_SCHEMA_SUFFIX', '') }}"
          http_scheme: https
          session_properties:
            transformations: true
        
        prod:
          type: trino
          method: jwt
          user: "{{ env_var('DUNE_TEAM_NAME') }}"
          jwt_token: "{{ env_var('DUNE_API_KEY') }}"
          host: trino.api.dune.com
          port: 443
          database: dune
          schema: "{{ env_var('DUNE_TEAM_NAME') }}"
          http_scheme: https
          session_properties:
            transformations: true
    
      target: dev
    

The `transformations: true` session property is **required**. This tells Dune that you’re running data transformation operations that need write access.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#4-test-your-connection)

4\. Test Your Connection
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Copy

Ask AI

    # Install dbt dependencies
    uv run dbt deps
    
    # Test connection
    uv run dbt debug
    
    # Run your first model
    uv run dbt run
    
    # Run tests
    uv run dbt test
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#project-structure)

Project Structure
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The template repository follows standard dbt conventions:

Copy

Ask AI

    your-dbt-project/
    ├── models/
    │   ├── templates/          # Example models for each strategy
    │   │   ├── dbt_template_view_model.sql
    │   │   ├── dbt_template_table_model.sql
    │   │   ├── dbt_template_merge_incremental_model.sql
    │   │   ├── dbt_template_delete_insert_incremental_model.sql
    │   │   └── dbt_template_append_incremental_model.sql
    │   └── your_models/        # Your transformation models
    ├── macros/
    │   └── dune_dbt_overrides/
    │       └── get_custom_schema.sql  # Schema naming logic
    ├── tests/                  # Custom data tests
    ├── seeds/                  # CSV seed files
    ├── snapshots/              # Snapshot definitions
    ├── analyses/               # Ad-hoc analyses
    ├── .github/workflows/      # CI/CD workflows (disabled by default—see note above)
    ├── profiles.yml            # dbt connection profile
    ├── dbt_project.yml         # Project configuration
    └── README.md
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#schema-organization)

Schema Organization
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Schemas are automatically organized based on your dbt target:

| Target | DEV\_SCHEMA\_SUFFIX | Schema Name | Use Case |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `dev` | Not set | `{team}__tmp_` | Local development (default) |
| `dev` | Set to `alice` | `{team}__tmp_alice` | Personal dev space |
| `dev` | Set to `pr123` | `{team}__tmp_pr123` | CI/CD per PR |
| `prod` | (any) | `{team}` | Production tables |

This is controlled by the `get_custom_schema.sql` macro in the template.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#how-it-works)

How It Works
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#namespace-isolation)

Namespace Isolation

All tables and views you create are organized into your team’s namespace:

*   **Production schema**: `{your_team}` - For production tables
*   **Development schemas**: `{your_team}__tmp_*` - For development and testing

This ensures complete isolation between teams and between development/production environments.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#write-operations)

Write Operations

Execute SQL statements to create and manage your data:

1.  **Create tables and views** in your namespace
2.  **Insert, update, or merge** data using standard SQL
3.  **Drop tables** when no longer needed
4.  **Optimize and vacuum** tables for optimal performance when querying these tables

All operations are authenticated via your Dune API key and restricted to your team’s namespace.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#data-access)

Data Access

**What You Can Read:**

*   **All public Dune datasets**: Full access to blockchain data across all supported chains
*   **Your uploaded data**: Private datasets you’ve uploaded to Dune
*   **Your transformation outputs**: Tables and views created in your namespace
*   **Materialized views**: Views that are materialized as tables in your namespace via the APP

**What You Can Write:**

*   **Your team namespace**: `{team_name}` for production tables
*   **Development namespaces**: `{team_name}__tmp_*` for dev and testing
*   **Private by default**: All created tables are private unless explicitly made public

**Access Control:**

*   Write operations are restricted to your team’s namespaces only
*   Cannot write to public schemas or other teams’ namespaces
*   Schema naming rules enforced: no `__tmp_` in team handles

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#querying-dbt-models-on-dune)

Querying dbt Models on Dune
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When querying your dbt models in the Dune app or via the API, you **must** use the `dune.` catalog prefix.

**Pattern**: `dune.{schema}.{table}`

Copy

Ask AI

    -- ❌ Won't work (dbt logs show this but it won't work on Dune)
    SELECT * FROM my_team.my_model
    
    -- ✅ Correct
    SELECT * FROM dune.my_team.my_model
    SELECT * FROM dune.my_team__tmp_alice.dev_model
    

dbt logs omit the catalog name for readability, so remember to add `dune.` when using queries in the Dune app.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#where-your-data-appears)

Where Your Data Appears
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Tables and views created through dbt appear in the **Data Explorer** under: **My Data → Connectors** ![Data Transformations in Data Explorer under Connectors](https://mintcdn.com/dune/Hf9LNgq7l6rcjPCE/images/data-transformations-explorer.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=Hf9LNgq7l6rcjPCE&q=85&s=b5e29cd9a75b97d667c2060453eb10b2) You can:

*   Browse your transformation datasets
*   View table schemas and metadata
*   Delete datasets directly from the UI
*   Search and reference them in queries

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/getting-started#next-steps)

Next Steps
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

------------------\
\
Learn about merge, delete+insert, and append strategies](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models)
[CI/CD & Workflows\
-----------------\
\
Set up GitHub Actions and development workflows](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/cicd-workflows)

# Incremental Models - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Transform your Data

Incremental Models

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [1\. Merge Strategy (Recommended)](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#1-merge-strategy-recommended)
    
*   [2\. Delete+Insert Strategy](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#2-delete%2Binsert-strategy)
    
*   [3\. Append Strategy](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#3-append-strategy)
    
*   [Strategy Comparison](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#strategy-comparison)
    
*   [Table Maintenance](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#table-maintenance)
    
*   [Manual Maintenance](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#manual-maintenance)
    
*   [Automated Maintenance with dbt post-hooks](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#automated-maintenance-with-dbt-post-hooks)
    
*   [Project level post-hooks](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#project-level-post-hooks)
    
*   [Dropping Tables](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#dropping-tables)
    
*   [Option 1: Use dbt’s —full-refresh flag then remove the model](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#option-1-use-dbt%E2%80%99s-%E2%80%94full-refresh-flag-then-remove-the-model)
    
*   [Option 2: Connect with a SQL client](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#option-2-connect-with-a-sql-client)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#examples)
    

dbt supports multiple strategies for incremental models. The template includes examples of each strategy to help you get started.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#1-merge-strategy-recommended)

1\. Merge Strategy (Recommended)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**When to use**: When you need to update existing rows and insert new ones. **Example**:

Copy

Ask AI

    {{
        config(
            materialized='incremental',
            unique_key='user_address',
            incremental_strategy='merge'
        )
    }}
    
    SELECT
        user_address,
        COUNT(*) as trade_count,
        SUM(volume_usd) as total_volume,
        MAX(block_time) as last_trade_time
    FROM {{ source('ethereum', 'dex_trades') }}
    WHERE block_time >= date_trunc('day', now() - interval '1' day)
    {% if is_incremental() %}
        AND block_time >= (SELECT MAX(last_trade_time) FROM {{ this }})
    {% endif %}
    GROUP BY 1
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#2-delete+insert-strategy)

2\. Delete+Insert Strategy
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**When to use**: When recomputing entire partitions (e.g., daily aggregations). **Example**:

Copy

Ask AI

    {{
        config(
            materialized='incremental',
            unique_key='date',
            incremental_strategy='delete+insert'
        )
    }}
    
    SELECT
        date_trunc('day', block_time) as date,
        protocol,
        COUNT(*) as transaction_count,
        SUM(amount_usd) as volume
    FROM {{ source('ethereum', 'decoded_events') }}
    WHERE block_time >= date_trunc('day', now() - interval '7' day)
    {% if is_incremental() %}
        AND date_trunc('day', block_time) >= date_trunc('day', now() - interval '1' day)
    {% endif %}
    GROUP BY 1, 2
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#3-append-strategy)

3\. Append Strategy
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**When to use**: For immutable event logs that only need new rows appended. **Example**:

Copy

Ask AI

    {{
        config(
            materialized='incremental',
            unique_key='tx_hash',
            incremental_strategy='append'
        )
    }}
    
    SELECT
        tx_hash,
        block_time,
        block_number,
        "from" as from_address,
        "to" as to_address,
        value
    FROM {{ source('ethereum', 'transactions') }}
    WHERE block_time >= date_trunc('hour', now() - interval '1' hour)
    {% if is_incremental() %}
        AND block_time >= (SELECT MAX(block_time) FROM {{ this }})
    {% endif %}
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#strategy-comparison)

Strategy Comparison
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

| Strategy | Best For | How It Works |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Merge** | Updating existing rows + inserting new | Matches on `unique_key`, updates existing, inserts new |
| **Delete+Insert** | Recomputing partitions | Deletes matching rows, then inserts new data |
| **Append** | Immutable event logs | Only inserts new rows, no updates or deletes |

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#table-maintenance)

Table Maintenance
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Maintenance operations consume credits based on compute and data written. These operations are necessary to keep your tables performant and to reclaim storage space.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#manual-maintenance)

Manual Maintenance

Run OPTIMIZE and VACUUM to improve performance and reduce storage costs:

Copy

Ask AI

    # Optimize a specific table
    uv run dbt run-operation optimize_table --args '{table_name: "my_model"}'
    
    # Vacuum a specific table
    uv run dbt run-operation vacuum_table --args '{table_name: "my_model"}'
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#automated-maintenance-with-dbt-post-hooks)

Automated Maintenance with dbt post-hooks

Add post-hooks to your model configuration:

Copy

Ask AI

    {{
        config(
            materialized='incremental',
            post_hook=[\
                "ALTER TABLE {{ this }} EXECUTE OPTIMIZE",\
                "ALTER TABLE {{ this }} EXECUTE VACUUM"\
            ]
        )
    }}
    
    SELECT ...
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#project-level-post-hooks)

Project level post-hooks

Add post-hooks to your project configuration:

Copy

Ask AI

    # dbt_project.yml
    post-hooks:
      - "ALTER TABLE {{ this }} EXECUTE OPTIMIZE"
      - "ALTER TABLE {{ this }} EXECUTE VACUUM"
    

The [template repository](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template)
 includes a default post-hook that runs OPTIMIZE and VACUUM on all tables.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#dropping-tables)

Dropping Tables
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

dbt doesn’t have a built-in way to drop tables. Options:

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#option-1-use-dbt%E2%80%99s-%E2%80%94full-refresh-flag-then-remove-the-model)

Option 1: Use dbt’s —full-refresh flag then remove the model

Copy

Ask AI

    # This will drop and recreate
    uv run dbt run --select my_model --full-refresh
    
    # Then delete the model file and run again
    rm models/my_model.sql
    uv run dbt run
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#option-2-connect-with-a-sql-client)

Option 2: Connect with a SQL client

Use any Trino-compatible client (Hex, Jupyter, DBeaver) to execute:

Copy

Ask AI

    DROP TABLE IF EXISTS dune.your_team.old_model;
    

See the [SQL Operations Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/sql-operations)
 for details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/incremental-models#examples)

Examples
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Complete examples are available in the template repository:

*   **View Model**: Lightweight, always fresh data
*   **Table Model**: Static snapshots for specific points in time
*   **Merge Incremental**: Update existing rows, insert new ones
*   **Delete+Insert Incremental**: Recompute partitions efficiently
*   **Append Incremental**: Add-only with deduplication

[dbt Template Repository\
-----------------------\
\
See all example models in our official dbt template repository](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-dbt-template)

YesNo

Navigation

BI Visualization Tools

Trino SDKs

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
