On this page

*   [Code Examples](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/sdks#code-examples)
    
*   [Connection Parameters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/sdks#connection-parameters)
    

Connect to Dune using Trino SDKs in your preferred language. Dune supports any Trino, Presto, or Starburst-compatible client library.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/sdks#code-examples)

Code Examples
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Bash
    
*   TypeScript
    
*   Python
    
*   Rust
    
*   Go
    
*   Ruby
    

Copy

Ask AI

    # Install: brew install trino
    trino --server https://trino.api.dune.com:443 \
      --user dune --password \
      --catalog delta_prod \
      --schema runtime \
      --execute "SELECT count(*) FROM base.transactions WHERE block_time > now() - interval '1' day"
    

Copy

Ask AI

    import { Trino, BasicAuth } from "trino-client";
    
    const trino = Trino.create({
      server: "https://trino.api.dune.com:443",
      catalog: "delta_prod",
      schema: "runtime",
      auth: new BasicAuth("dune", process.env.DUNE_API_KEY),
    });
    
    const iter = await trino.query("SELECT count(*) FROM base.transactions WHERE block_time > now() - interval '1' day");
    for await (const result of iter) {
      console.log(result.data);
    }
    

Copy

Ask AI

    import trino
    import os
    
    conn = trino.dbapi.connect(
        host='trino.api.dune.com',
        port=443,
        user='dune',
        catalog='delta_prod',
        schema='runtime',
        auth=trino.auth.BasicAuthentication('dune', os.environ['DUNE_API_KEY']),
        http_scheme='https'
    )
    
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    cursor.execute("SELECT count(*) FROM base.transactions WHERE block_time > now() - interval '1' day")
    print(cursor.fetchall())
    

Copy

Ask AI

    use prusto::{ClientBuilder, Presto};
    
    #[derive(Presto, Debug)]
    struct Foo {
        a: i64,
        b: f64,
        c: String,
    }
    
    #[tokio::main]
    async fn main() {
        let cli = ClientBuilder::new("user", "localhost")
            .port(8090)
            .catalog("catalog")
            .build()
            .unwrap();
    
        let sql = "select 1 as a, cast(1.1 as double) as b, 'bar' as c ";
    
        let data = cli.get_all::<Foo>(sql.into()).await.unwrap().into_vec();
    
        for r in data {
            println!("{:?}", r)
        }
    }
    

Copy

Ask AI

    import "database/sql"
    import _ "github.com/trinodb/trino-go-client/trino"
    
    dsn := "http://user@localhost:8080?catalog=default&schema=test"
    db, err := sql.Open("trino", dsn)
    

Copy

Ask AI

    require 'trino-client'
    
    # create a client object:
    client = Trino::Client.new(
      server: "localhost:8880",   # required option
      ssl: {verify: false},
      catalog: "native",
      schema: "default",
      user: "frsyuki",
      password: "********",
      time_zone: "US/Pacific",
      language: "English",
      properties: {
        "hive.force_local_scheduling": true,
        "raptor.reader_stream_buffer_size": "32MB"
      },
      http_proxy: "proxy.example.com:8080",
      http_debug: true
    )
    
    # run a query and get results as an array of arrays:
    columns, rows = client.run("select * from sys.node")
    rows.each {|row|
      p row  # row is an array
    }
    
    # run a query and get results as an array of hashes:
    results = client.run_with_names("select alpha, 1 AS beta from tablename")
    results.each {|row|
      p row['alpha']   # access by name
      p row['beta']
      p row.values[0]  # access by index
      p row.values[1]
    }
    
    # run a query and fetch results streamingly:
    client.query("select * from sys.node") do |q|
      # get columns:
      q.columns.each {|column|
        puts "column: #{column.name}.#{column.type}"
      }
    
      # get query results. it feeds more rows until
      # query execution finishes:
      q.each_row {|row|
        p row  # row is an array
      }
    end
    
    # killing a query
    query = client.query("select * from sys.node")
    query_id = query.query_info.query_id
    query.each_row {|row| ... }  # when a thread is processing the query,
    client.kill(query_id)  # another thread / process can kill the query.
    
    # Use Query#transform_row to parse Trino ROW types into Ruby Hashes.
    # You can also set a scalar_parser to parse scalars how you'd like them.
    scalar_parser = -> (data, type) { (type === 'json') ? JSON.parse(data) : data }
    client.query("select * from sys.node") do |q|
      q.scalar_parser = scalar_parser
    
      # get query results. it feeds more rows until
      # query execution finishes:
      q.each_row {|row|
        p q.transform_row(row)
      }
    end
    

Besides the code samples shown above, Trino supports a variety of other official and unofficial SDKs. Please check the [official Trino SDKs page](https://trino.io/ecosystem/client-driver#official-client-drivers)
 to see which ones are available and to view their GitHub repositories for updated code samples and documentation.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/sdks#connection-parameters)

Connection Parameters
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For all SDK integrations, use the following connection parameters:

| Parameter | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Host | `trino.api.dune.com` |
| Port | `443` |
| Username | `dune` |
| Password | Your Dune API key |
| Catalog | `delta_prod` |
| HTTP scheme | `https` |

See the [Overview](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview#connection-parameters)
 for complete connection details.

# Dune MCP - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Agents

Dune MCP

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Connect Dune MCP](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#connect-dune-mcp)
    
*   [Claude Code](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#claude-code)
    
*   [Claude Desktop / Web App](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#claude-desktop-%2F-web-app)
    
*   [OpenCode](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#opencode)
    
*   [Codex](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#codex)
    
*   [Cursor](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#cursor)
    
*   [ChatGPT](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#chatgpt)
    
*   [Key Benefits](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#key-benefits)
    
*   [Use Cases](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#use-cases)
    

MCP (Model Context Protocol) is an open-source standard for connecting AI applications to external systems. Dune MCP gives your agent direct, structured access to Dune workflows: discover the right tables, create and run queries, inspect results, and create visualizations in the same conversation. This is the fastest way to move from prompt to reliable onchain analysis. Dune MCP currently ships with these official tools:

| Category | Tool | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Discovery** | `searchDocs` | Search Dune docs for guides, examples, and API references |
| **Discovery** | `searchTables` | Find tables by protocol, chain, category, or schema |
| **Discovery** | `listBlockchains` | List indexed blockchains with table counts |
| **Discovery** | `searchTablesByContractAddress` | Find decoded event/call tables for a contract address |
| **Query Lifecycle** | `createDuneQuery` | Create and save a new Dune query |
| **Query Lifecycle** | `getDuneQuery` | Fetch SQL and metadata for an existing query |
| **Query Lifecycle** | `updateDuneQuery` | Update SQL, title, description, tags, or parameters |
| **Query Lifecycle** | `executeQueryById` | Execute a saved query and return an execution ID |
| **Query Lifecycle** | `getExecutionResults` | Fetch status and results for a query execution |
| **Visualization** | `generateVisualization` | Create charts, counters, and tables from query results |
| **Account** | `getUsage` | Check current billing-period credit usage |

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#connect-dune-mcp)

Connect Dune MCP
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All clients authenticate to Dune MCP with your [Dune API key](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/authentication)
.

*   MCP endpoint: `https://api.dune.com/mcp/v1`
*   Header auth: `x-dune-api-key: <dune-api-key>`
*   Query auth (for clients that prefer URL auth): `?api_key=<dune_api_key>`

OAuth with your Dune account is coming soon. For now, authenticate with a Dune API key.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#claude-code)

Claude Code

Copy

Ask AI

    claude mcp add --scope user --transport http dune https://api.dune.com/mcp/v1 --header "x-dune-api-key: <dune-api-key>"
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#claude-desktop-/-web-app)

Claude Desktop / Web App

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#opencode)

OpenCode

![Connect opencode to Dune MCP](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uuYoKpKP5Xcm0UmT/images/open_code.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=uuYoKpKP5Xcm0UmT&q=85&s=2ecc4eb1cd8cba85c51ccb95b99447c9)

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#codex)

Codex

Copy

Ask AI

    codex mcp add dune_prod --url "https://api.dune.com/mcp/v1?api_key=<dune_api_key>"
    

**Known issue: “Transport closed” errors during long-running queries**Codex’s MCP client has a default tool timeout of 60 seconds. When `getExecutionResults` polls for a query that takes longer than this, Codex terminates the connection. Due to a [known Codex bug](https://github.com/openai/codex/issues/11489)
, the MCP transport does not auto-reconnect after a timeout — all subsequent tool calls will fail with `Transport closed` until you start a new session.**Workaround:** Increase the Codex tool timeout in your config:

Copy

Ask AI

    [mcp_servers.dune]
    url = "https://api.dune.com/mcp/v1?api_key=<dune_api_key>"
    tool_timeout_sec = 300
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#cursor)

Cursor

Add this configuration to your Cursor settings:

Copy

Ask AI

    {
      "mcpServers": {
        "dune": {
          "url": "https://api.dune.com/mcp/v1",
          "headers": {
            "X-DUNE-API-KEY": "<api_key>"
          }
        }
      }
    }
    

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#chatgpt)

ChatGPT

ChatGPT support is planned via OAuth and will be documented here once available.

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#key-benefits)

Key Benefits
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Natural Language to SQL
-----------------------

Describe the question in plain English and let your agent discover tables, draft SQL, and return results.

Cross-Chain Coverage
--------------------

Work across Dune’s indexed chains through one MCP interface, with discovery and query tools in the same flow.

End-to-End Workflow
-------------------

Go from question to execution to visualization in one conversation without switching apps.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp#use-cases)

Use Cases
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

Protocol Analytics
------------------

Track core metrics like volume, users, or activity using curated and decoded datasets.

Wallet Intelligence
-------------------

Analyze wallet behavior, holdings, and flows across multiple chains from a single prompt.

Market Research
---------------

Compare sectors, tokens, and venues with reusable query and visualization workflows.

Data Workflow Prototyping
-------------------------

Iterate quickly on query ideas, validate results, and turn them into saved assets.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Build Custom Dashboards & Reports](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/apis/quickstart-dashboards)
[CLI & Skills](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/cli-and-skills)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

*   Retrieve detailed information about a specific dataset by its slug - Returns complete schema including all columns with data types - Includes ownership details and metadata - Example slugs: `dex.trades`, `tokens.erc20`, `ethereum.transactions`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/get#use-cases)

Use Cases
=====================================================================================

*   **Schema Discovery**: Retrieve the complete schema of a dataset including column names, data types, and nullability.
*   **Table Exploration**: Understand the structure of a dataset before writing queries against it.
*   **Data Integration**: Programmatically fetch table schemas for ETL pipelines and data integration tools.
*   **Documentation Generation**: Automatically generate documentation for datasets based on their schemas.
*   **Validation**: Verify dataset structure and columns before building queries or applications.

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/get#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/get#parameter-slug)

slug

string

required

Dataset slug (e.g., 'dex.trades')

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/get#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

#### Response

application/json

OK

object\[\]

Show child attributes

string

full\_name

string

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/get#response-is-private)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/get#response-metadata)

object

Show child attributes

string

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#use-cases)

Use Cases
======================================================================================

*   **Browse Available Data**: Programmatically discover all tables and datasets available on Dune for querying.
*   **Filter by Owner**: Find all datasets owned by a specific user or team using `owner_handle` parameter.
*   **Filter by Type**: Narrow down results to specific dataset types like curated tables, decoded tables, or transformations using the `type` parameter.
*   **Build Data Catalogs**: Create custom data discovery tools that index and search through Dune’s table ecosystem.
*   **Access Management**: Audit and manage datasets owned by your team or organization.

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Number of results to return (default 50, max 250)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset for pagination

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#parameter-owner-handle)

owner\_handle

string

Filter by owner handle

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#parameter-type)

type

string

Filter by dataset types (comma-separated: transformation\_view, transformation\_table, uploaded\_table, decoded\_table, spell, dune\_table)

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#response-datasets)

datasets

object\[\]

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/datasets/endpoint/list#response-total)

total

integer

# Products Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Products Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Capabilities](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#capabilities)
    
*   [Query & Architecture](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#query-%26-architecture)
    
*   [Data Coverage](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#data-coverage)
    
*   [Interface & Pricing](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#interface-%26-pricing)
    
*   [Quick Selection Guide](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#quick-selection-guide)
    

Dune delivers blockchain data via three core products: **Data Hub**, **Datashare**, and **Sim (Realtime APIs)**. Each product serves different use cases, from ad-hoc analytics to real-time wallet application development.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#capabilities)

Capabilities
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

What each product is best suited for.

|     | [Data Hub](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview) | [Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare) | [Sim (Realtime APIs)](https://sim.dune.com/) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Best For** | Primary onchain data warehouse, Analytic workflows, [Data transformations](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview) | Data warehouse integration & Interoperability | Build realtime wallets, portfolio apps |
| **SQL Access** | ✓ Full SQL | ✓ Full SQL | REST APIs |
| **Historical Data** | ✓ Full historical | ✓ Full historical | Realtime |
| **Authentication** | Dune account, API key | Warehouse credentials | Sim account, API key |

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#query-&-architecture)

Query & Architecture
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

How each product handles queries and processes data under the hood.

|     | [Data Hub](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview) | [Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare) | [Sim (Realtime APIs)](https://sim.dune.com/) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Query Infra** | DuneSQL / Trino | Snowflake, BigQuery, Databricks | N/A |
| **Query Speed** | ~3 seconds | N/A | N/A |
| **Engine** | Custom Trino (Small, Medium, Large) | N/A | N/A |
| **Architecture** | OLAP, Delta parquet | OLAP, mostly Iceberg parquet | Real-time |

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#data-coverage)

Data Coverage
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

What data is available and how fresh it is across each product.

|     | [Data Hub](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview) | [Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare) | [Sim (Realtime APIs)](https://sim.dune.com/) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Freshness** | EVM: ~1-15 min  <br>Solana: ~1-5 min  <br>Curated: ~1 hour | Hourly or daily | < 1 second |
| **Blockchains** | [100+ chains](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/overview) | [100+ chains](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/overview) | 60+ chains |
| **Schemas** | [Raw](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/ethereum/raw/transactions)<br>, [Decoded](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/ethereum/decoded/overview)<br>, Curated ([DEX Trades](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/curated/dex-trades)<br>, [Prices](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/curated/prices)<br>, [Token Transfers](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/curated/token-transfers/overview)<br>, [more](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/curated/overview)<br>) | Same as Data Hub | Curated (Balances, Activity, DeFi, Token Info) |

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#interface-&-pricing)

Interface & Pricing
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

How you access each product and pricing.

|     | [Data Hub](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview) | [Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare) | [Sim (Realtime APIs)](https://sim.dune.com/) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Interface** | [Dune App](https://dune.com/)<br>, [Data API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/api-overview)<br>, [External BI Tools](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview) | [BigQuery](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare-bigquery)<br>, [Snowflake](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare-snowflake)<br>, [Databricks](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare-databricks) | REST APIs |
| **Pricing** | Credits (compute-based) | Flat Subscription Fees | API Call Volume (CUs) |

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/product-comparison#quick-selection-guide)

Quick Selection Guide
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Data Hub\
--------\
\
**Best for:** Your primary onchain data warehouse, analytic workflows, and data transformationsFull SQL access with 100+ chains, flexible schemas, and compute-based pricing](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Datashare\
---------\
\
**Best for:** Data warehouse integration and interoperabilityDirect access via Snowflake, BigQuery, or Databricks with full historical data](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Sim (Realtime APIs)\
-------------------\
\
**Best for:** Building realtime wallets, portfolio trackers, and DeFi applicationsSub-second response times with 60+ chains via REST APIs](https://sim.dune.com/)
[Catalyst\
--------\
\
**Best for:** Blockchain integration and data infrastructureDune’s toolkit for chains and protocols to get indexed and make their data accessible](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

**Why is Catalyst not in the comparison tables?** Catalyst is Dune’s blockchain integration toolkit designed for chains and protocols, not end-user data consumption. It powers how blockchains get indexed into Dune rather than how users query data, so it serves a fundamentally different purpose than Data Hub, Datashare, and Sim (Realtime APIs).

YesNo

[Introduction](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Sim (Realtime APIs)](https://docs.dune.com/docs/sim-real-time-apis)

Analytics teams use Dune’s enriched data, query interface, and visualization layer to understand blockchain ecosystems, track protocol performance, analyze market trends, and generate insights from onchain activity.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/analytics#common-use-cases)

Common Use Cases
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Protocol Metrics
----------------

Track TVL, user activity, revenue, and ecosystem growth for protocols and DAOs

Trading Intelligence
--------------------

Analyze DEX volumes, token flows, whale movements, and market trends

Stablecoin & Payments Intelligence
----------------------------------

Flow analysis, payment tracking, peg stability, and adoption metrics

Ecosystem Benchmarking
----------------------

Competitive analysis, market positioning, and chain comparisons

User Behavior Analytics
-----------------------

Wallet activity patterns, cohort analysis, retention, and user journeys

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/analytics#who-this-is-for)

Who This Is For
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Protocols & DAOs
----------------

Track TVL, user activity, and ecosystem metrics to inform product and governance decisions

L1s, L2s & Appchains
--------------------

Monitor network health, adoption, developer activity, and ecosystem growth

Trading & Research Teams
------------------------

Analyze DEX volumes, token flows, and market dynamics for trading strategies

Investment Research
-------------------

Track portfolio performance, analyze market trends, and identify opportunities

Stablecoins

Monitor flows, peg stability, adoption metrics, and payment volumes

FiltersClear

New releasesImprovements

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#product-updates)

Product updates
============================================================================

> New releases and improvements

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#february-2026)

February 2026

New releasesImprovements

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#dune-mcp)

Dune MCP
--------------------------------------------------------------

We launched the Dune MCP (Model Context Protocol), enabling AI agents to query, execute, and interact with Dune directly. Connect the MCP to Claude, Cursor, or any compatible AI agent and let it search tables, execute queries, generate visualizations, and more — all without leaving your workflow. See the [MCP documentation](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/agents/mcp)
 for setup instructions.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#defi-positions-api)

DeFi Positions API
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The DeFi Positions API is now available on [Sim](https://docs.sim.dune.com/evm/defi-positions)
. Get a wallet’s active DeFi positions — liquidity pools, lending, and yield strategies — with USD valuations and protocol metadata. Supports Uniswap V2/V3/V4 (and forks), Aave v2/v3, and ERC-4626 vaults across 9 EVM chains.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#stablecoin-dataset-&-showcase-page)

Stablecoin Dataset & Showcase Page
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A first-class stablecoin analytics product built on 346 SQL models across 38 chains. The classification layer matches every transfer to its onchain trigger (DEX swap, lending event, bridge deposit, CEX movement) and labels every holder address by venue type. Premium tables include `activity_enriched` and `balances_enriched` for EVM and Solana. Free foundation tables — `transfers` and `balances` — are available for EVM, Solana, and Tron. Explore the [Stablecoin Showcase](https://dune.com/collection/stablecoins/overview)
 or see the [Stablecoins documentation](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/curated/stablecoins/overview)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#raw-solana-data-in-bigquery-us-datashare)

Raw Solana Data in BigQuery US (Datashare)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All raw Solana data is now synced to BigQuery in the US region via Datashare — over 600TB across 9 tables including `solana.account_activity`, `solana.instruction_calls`, `solana.transactions`, and more. Existing US multi-region customers can access this data at no extra cost.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#credit-based-pricing-model)

Credit-Based Pricing Model
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

We’ve transitioned all self-serve plans to the new credit-based pricing model. This update consolidates exports, writes, and storage under a single credit-based system, removing datapoint conversions and simplifying billing. See [Billing](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/billing)
 for details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#datasets-in-discover)

Datasets in Discover
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Shipped [dune.com/discover/data](https://dune.com/discover/data)
 to surface Datasets in the Discover page. Browse and search curated datasets with chain coverage badges and direct links to documentation — part of a broader effort to drive visibility and traffic to Dune’s data products.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#sidebar-navigation-redesign)

Sidebar Navigation Redesign
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Elevated key pages from Library to the primary sidebar on dune.com. Dashboards, Queries, Schedules, Alerts, Uploaded data, Materialized views, Connectors, Custom endpoints, Folders, Contracts, and APIs are now directly accessible from the sidebar, making it easier to find and manage your content.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#improvements)

Improvements
----------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Pie chart upgrade** — New color palette with blockchain color mapping, redesigned tooltips, and adjusted legend layout, bringing pie charts on par with other chart types
*   **Chart duplicate x handling** — New chart option to visualize and control how duplicate x values within a series are handled, with options to sum across duplicates
*   **9 new Solana DEX AMMs** — Added 9 new projects to `dex_solana.trades` under a unified prop AMM design
*   **Usage activity table** — The usage table now persists all modifications (search, filter, columns, sorting, pagination, time range) in the URL, so you can bookmark and share filtered views
*   **Datashare status page** — Datashare now has its own section on the [Dune status page](https://status.dune.com/)
     with per-target data warehouse status monitoring

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#january-2026)

January 2026

New releasesImprovements

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#incremental-queries)

Incremental Queries
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Incremental Queries allow you to write SQL that processes only recent data and merges it with previous query results. This enables fresh data analysis at a fraction of the cost, making it ideal for dashboards and reports that need regular updates. The feature supports complex queries including group bys and cumulative sums. See the [Incremental Queries documentation](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/incremental-queries)
 for details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#mermaid-charts-in-dashboards)

Mermaid Charts in Dashboards
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can now create Mermaid diagrams directly in dashboard text widgets. Use the `mermaid` code block syntax to add flowcharts, sequence diagrams, and other visualizations to your dashboards.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#new-curated-table-tokens-fdv_latest)

New Curated Table: tokens.fdv\_latest
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A new curated table for Fully Diluted Valuation (FDV) data across all EVM chains. The table shows ERC20 tokens with onchain transfers, their latest supply (updated on mint/burn events), and FDV calculated. This table is in open beta as we continue to work and improve it.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#data-sources-visibility)

Data Sources Visibility
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Queries now display their data sources in the sidebar. Additionally Dashboards include a new “Data” button showing all datasets used to build the dashboard.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#dbt-connector-video-tutorial)

dbt Connector Video Tutorial
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A new [video tutorial](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TRqqPC0PcZU)
 for the dbt Connector is now available, providing step-by-step guidance for setting up and using dbt on Dune.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#improvements-2)

Improvements
------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Dune AI** — Improved Dune AI with a modern agentic approach for better query generation and assistance
*   **Curated Data Explorer** — Reorganized curated data section with revamped categories and a new “More curated data” section
*   **Okta real-time sync (Enterprise)** — Users removed from an Okta organization are now immediately logged out of Dune
*   **Dashboard timestamps** — Dashboards now display “updated at” timestamps instead of “created at” on profile pages
*   **Simplified authentication** — Removed “Sign in with Ethereum” option to streamline the login experience (wallet linking remains available after signup)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#december-2025)

December 2025

New releasesImprovements

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#domain-restricted-google-sso-enterprise)

Domain-Restricted Google SSO (Enterprise)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Team admins can now enable domain restriction via Google SSO in team settings. This forces team members to log in using their company email (e.g., @company.com), preventing non-employees from accessing the workspace. When enabled, all team members are logged out and must re-authenticate with Google SSO. See the [Google SSO documentation](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction)
 for setup details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#okta-sso-enterprise)

Okta SSO (Enterprise)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

We now support Okta SSO for Enterprise customers, a frequently requested feature for enterprise security requirements. You can enable Okta SSO via team settings under the new “Settings & Privacy” tab. We also extended this feature to support multiple domains for organizations with complex Okta tenant configurations. See the [Okta SSO documentation](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso)
 for setup details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#usage-table)

Usage Table
--------------------------------------------------------------------

A new Usage table is now available, containing records of metered App, API, and Connector events. Users can search, filter, and export these records for detailed usage analysis and cost tracking.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#private-content-by-default-enterprise)

Private Content by Default (Enterprise)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Enterprise customers can now control the default privacy mode for team content with three options:

*   **Public by default** — Team members choose per content
*   **Private by default** — New content defaults to private, can be made public individually
*   **Private only** — All content forced private, external sharing disabled

This helps teams working with sensitive data ensure privacy is the default, making link sharing an explicit opt-in.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#improvements-3)

Improvements
------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Export CSV downloads** — Improved CSV export experience for usage data
*   **Folder filtering** — Filter by Dashboards or Queries inside folders
*   **Embed fix** — Fixed an issue where embeds did not show username/avatar when the query belonged to a user
*   **EVM Contract resubmission** — Resubmission actions (rename, upgrade, delete) now gated to paid team plans
*   **Query editor UX** — Click the drag icon to expand the query editor (in addition to dragging)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#november-2025)

November 2025

New releasesImprovements

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#databricks-support-for-datashare-enterprise)

Databricks Support for Datashare (Enterprise)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Datashare now supports Databricks, expanding our data warehouse integrations beyond Snowflake and BigQuery. Stream Dune’s complete blockchain dataset directly into your Databricks environment. See the [Databricks documentation](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare-databricks)
 and read the [announcement blog post](https://dune.com/blog/expanding-dune-datashare-with-databricks)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#dbt-connector-enterprise)

dbt Connector (Enterprise)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Enterprise customers can now use dbt for in-platform data transformations with incremental runs. Build production data pipelines, version control your models, and run transformations directly on Dune. See the [dbt Connector documentation](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview)
 and read the [announcement blog post](https://dune.com/blog/run-dbt-on-dune-your-crypto-data-warehouse)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#new-chain-support)

New Chain Support
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Added support for [Initia](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/overview)
, [Kalshi](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview)
, [Story](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/story/overview)
, [Mezo](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/mezo/overview)
, and [Monad](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/monad/overview)
. Explore raw, decoded, and curated data for these new chains in the Data Catalog.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#new-api-landing-page)

New API Landing Page
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A new [API landing page](https://dune.com/apis)
 provides a unified view of all endpoints with quick curl/preview actions and documentation links.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#new-api-endpoints)

New API Endpoints
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

New endpoints for executing arbitrary SQL, pipeline executions, usage data, and dataset metadata. See the [API documentation](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
 for details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/changelog#improvements-4)

Improvements
------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Improved usage overview** — Charts and copyable API keys for better visibility
*   **Increased max query result size** — From 8GB to 32GB
*   **Restructured [API documentation](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
    ** — Scannable for newcomers while keeping advanced details discoverable
*   **Updated SDKs** — All new endpoints included
*   **Deprecated `/v1/tables` endpoints** — Moved to `/v1/uploads`. See the [Tables API documentation](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/tables/endpoint/overview)
     for migration details

Data engineering teams use Dune to build production data pipelines, transform blockchain data, and integrate onchain insights into their applications and workflows.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/engineering#common-use-cases)

Common Use Cases
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Build Data Pipelines
--------------------

Create production-grade data models and transformation pipelines with dbt on Dune

Stream to Your Warehouse
------------------------

Export blockchain data to Snowflake, BigQuery, or Databricks via Datashare

Programmatic Access
-------------------

Execute queries, manage data, and integrate Dune into your applications via Data API

Power Wallet & App Backends
---------------------------

Build realtime wallet experiences and DeFi apps with sub-second latency via Sim APIs

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/engineering#who-this-is-for)

Who This Is For
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Data Engineering Teams
----------------------

Build and maintain data pipelines, models, and transformations on blockchain data

Wallets & Apps Engineering
--------------------------

Power wallet backends, portfolio trackers, and DeFi applications with onchain data

AI & Derived Analytics
----------------------

Build ML models, derived datasets, and AI-powered analytics on blockchain data

Product Teams
-------------

Integrate onchain data into product workflows, dashboards, and customer-facing features

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/engineering#how-it-works)

Accounting, audit, and compliance teams depend on Dune for transaction monitoring, data reconciliation, financial reporting, and AML investigations across blockchain networks.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/accounting-audit-aml#common-use-cases)

Common Use Cases
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Transaction Monitoring
----------------------

Track onchain transactions, wallet flows, and cross-chain movements for compliance

Account Reconciliation
----------------------

Verify token balances, staking positions, and DeFi holdings at any point in time

Financial Reporting
-------------------

Calculate realized gains/losses from DEX trades, staking rewards, and LP positions

Market Manipulation Detection
-----------------------------

Pump and dump analysis, wash trading on DEXs, prediction market wash trading, LP manipulation

AML & Fraud Investigation
-------------------------

Wallet clustering, sybil detection, sanctions screening, illicit fund tracing

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/accounting-audit-aml#who-this-is-for)

Who This Is For
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Accounting & Finance
--------------------

Transaction monitoring, reconciliation, and financial reporting for crypto treasuries

Risk & Compliance
-----------------

AML/KYC workflows, sanctions screening, and regulatory compliance monitoring

Brokerages & Exchanges
----------------------

Trade reconciliation, compliance reporting, and market surveillance

Custodians
----------

Asset verification, balance audits, and custody reporting

Professional Services
---------------------

Big 4 auditors, tax preparers, and consulting firms serving crypto clients

Public Sector
-------------

Regulators, policymakers, and government agencies monitoring crypto markets

[​](https://docs.dune.com/docs/use-cases/accounting-audit-aml#how-it-works)

# Data Hub Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#content-area)

Data Hub

Data Hub Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Prerequisites](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#prerequisites)
    
*   [What You Can Do](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#what-you-can-do)
    
*   [Quick Start](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#quick-start)
    
*   [Next Steps](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#next-steps)
    

The Data Hub is Dune’s web-based workspace where you query blockchain data with SQL, build visualizations, assemble dashboards, and share insights with your team or the public. It is one of several ways to work with Dune’s data — alongside the [Data API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/api-overview)
, [dbt integration](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/dbt/overview)
, [BI tool connectors](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/connectors/trino/overview)
, and [Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
. ![Data transformations on Dune](https://mintcdn.com/dune/7jTylmCpqk1GQLzb/images/data-transformations-dune.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=7jTylmCpqk1GQLzb&q=85&s=7dcdde0d99b2ec3a6a76fffc2b936ec7)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#prerequisites)

Prerequisites
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Dune Account:** [Sign up here](https://dune.com/auth/register)
     if you do not already have one.
*   **Basic SQL Knowledge:** Dune uses DuneSQL, a SQL dialect compatible with TrinoSQL. If you are new to SQL, [start here](https://www.w3schools.com/sql/)
    .

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#what-you-can-do)

What You Can Do
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Write and Run Queries\
---------------------\
\
Use the Query Editor to write SQL against blockchain data, add parameters, and schedule automated runs.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor)
[Visualize and Present Results\
-----------------------------\
\
Turn query results into charts, counters, tables, and interactive dashboards.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs)
[Automate and Monitor\
--------------------\
\
Schedule queries and dashboards to refresh automatically. Set up alerts for email or webhook notifications.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler)
[Share and Embed\
---------------\
\
Share dashboards by URL, embed live visualizations on any website, or export data via CSV and API.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/share)
[Import and Export Data\
----------------------\
\
Upload your own CSV datasets to join with blockchain data. Export query results in CSV or JSON.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/upload-data)
[Decode Smart Contracts\
----------------------\
\
Submit contracts for decoding to create structured, queryable tables from raw transaction bytecode.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts)
[Manage Your Team\
----------------\
\
Create team workspaces, assign roles, share credits, and configure SSO for your organization.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams)
[Search and Discover\
-------------------\
\
Find dashboards, queries, and analysts across Dune using search, discovery, and advanced filters.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/search)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#quick-start)

Quick Start
----------------------------------------------------------------------

Get from zero to a published dashboard in five minutes:

1.  **Create a query** — Open the [Query Editor](https://dune.com/queries)
     and write SQL. For example, daily Ethereum active addresses:

Copy

Ask AI

    SELECT
      date_trunc('day', block_time) AS time,
      COUNT(DISTINCT "from") AS active_senders
    FROM ethereum.transactions
    WHERE block_time > DATE '2024-01-01'
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1
    

2.  **Run and save** — Click **Run** to execute, then **Save** to persist your query.
3.  **Add a visualization** — Click **New Visualization**, choose a chart type, and configure your axes.
4.  **Build a dashboard** — Go to **Create > New Dashboard**, name it, then add your visualization as a widget.
5.  **Share it** — Copy the dashboard URL or use the **Share** button to embed it externally.

For a detailed walkthrough, see [Create Your First Query](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query)
 and [Create Your First Visualization](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-visualization)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview#next-steps)

Next Steps
--------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **[Query Templates](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates)
    :** Pre-built queries you can customize immediately.

    :** Explore all available blockchain data tables.

# Google SSO Domain Restriction - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Manage Your Team

Google SSO Domain Restriction

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [How the allowed domain is determined](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#how-the-allowed-domain-is-determined)
    
*   [What this setting does](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#what-this-setting-does)
    
*   [Before you enable this](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#before-you-enable-this)
    
*   [Enable Google SSO domain restriction](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#enable-google-sso-domain-restriction)
    

**Enterprise Feature** — Domain-restricted SSO is available on the [Enterprise plan](https://dune.com/enterprise)
. [Contact sales](https://dune.com/enterprise)
 to learn more.

Dune can restrict **Google SSO join requests** so that only users with an email address on an approved domain can join your team.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#how-the-allowed-domain-is-determined)

How the allowed domain is determined
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The **allowed domain is automatically set to the email domain of the team admin** who enables the setting. Example:

*   If the admin enabling the setting has `admin@dune.com`, then the allowed domain will be `dune.com`.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#what-this-setting-does)

What this setting does
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When enabled:

*   Only users signing in with Google SSO using the **allowed domain** can join the team.
*   Users attempting to join with a different email domain will be blocked.

This is useful to prevent personal Gmail accounts (or other unapproved domains) from joining your team.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#before-you-enable-this)

Before you enable this
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

> **Important:** You must remove any existing team members whose email domain does **not** match the admin’s domain **before** enabling this setting.

Also note:

*   While enabled, **users cannot change their email address** in Dune.
*   Users who previously used **email/password** will be prompted to sign in using **Google SSO**.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction#enable-google-sso-domain-restriction)

Enable Google SSO domain restriction
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Go to **Settings → Security & Privacy → Google SSO domain restriction**.
2.  Toggle **Restrict Google SSO** on.
3.  **Authenticate** your email domain.

Once enabled, Dune will display the allowed domain (for example: `dune.com`) in the setting.

[Okta SSO](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso)

# Okta SSO Setup - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Manage Your Team

Okta SSO Setup

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Prerequisites](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#prerequisites)
    
*   [Step 1 — Add and verify your SSO domain(s)](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-1-%E2%80%94-add-and-verify-your-sso-domains)
    
*   [Verify the domain (DNS TXT record)](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#verify-the-domain-dns-txt-record)
    
*   [Step 2 — Create an Okta OIDC app (Web)](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-2-%E2%80%94-create-an-okta-oidc-app-web)
    
*   [Step 3 — Copy Okta credentials into Dune](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-3-%E2%80%94-copy-okta-credentials-into-dune)
    
*   [Step 4 — Enable Okta SSO](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-4-%E2%80%94-enable-okta-sso)
    

**Enterprise Feature** — Okta SSO is available on the [Enterprise plan](https://dune.com/enterprise)
. [Contact sales](https://dune.com/enterprise)
 to learn more.

This guide walks you through enabling **Okta SSO** for your Dune team using **OIDC**.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#prerequisites)

Prerequisites
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

You’ll need:

*   Admin access for your **Dune team**
*   Admin access for your **Okta tenant**
*   Access to your domain’s **DNS provider** (to add TXT records)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-1-%E2%80%94-add-and-verify-your-sso-domains)

Step 1 — Add and verify your SSO domain(s)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  In Dune, go to **Settings → Security & Privacy → Okta authentication**.
2.  Under **Configure SSO domains**, click **Add domains**.
3.  Enter the email domain(s) your team uses (for example, `company.com`).

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#verify-the-domain-dns-txt-record)

Verify the domain (DNS TXT record)

After adding a domain, it may show as **Pending**. Dune will display DNS instructions like:

*   **Host**: `dune-verification`
*   **Type**: `TXT`
*   **Value**: a unique verification token

Add a TXT record in your DNS provider:

*   **Name / Host**: `dune-verification` (some providers require the full name like `dune-verification.company.com`)
*   **Type**: `TXT`
*   **Value**: (paste the token from Dune exactly)

Then return to Dune and click **Verify** next to the domain.

> **Tip** DNS changes can take time to propagate. If verification fails, double-check the host/name formatting in your DNS provider and try again after propagation.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-2-%E2%80%94-create-an-okta-oidc-app-web)

Step 2 — Create an Okta OIDC app (Web)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In Okta:

1.  Go to **Applications → Create App Integration**.
2.  Choose **OIDC - OpenID Connect**.
3.  Choose **Web Application**.
4.  In the app settings, add the **Sign-in redirect URIs** shown in Dune.
5.  Save the app.

> **Note** Use the redirect URIs **exactly** as shown in Dune. A mismatch is the most common cause of Okta sign-in errors.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-3-%E2%80%94-copy-okta-credentials-into-dune)

Step 3 — Copy Okta credentials into Dune
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Back in Dune (**Settings → Security & Privacy → Okta authentication**), fill in:

*   **Client ID**: from your Okta OIDC application
*   **Client secret**: from your Okta OIDC application
*   **Okta domain**: your Okta org URL, for example:
    *   `https://your-domain.okta.com`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/okta-sso#step-4-%E2%80%94-enable-okta-sso)

Step 4 — Enable Okta SSO
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Make sure at least one domain shows as **Verified**.
2.  Toggle **Enable Okta SSO** on.
3.  Click **Enable**.

> **Important**
> 
> *   Existing members with **non-matching domains must be removed** before enabling.
> *   Users **cannot change their email** while Okta SSO is enforced.
> *   Users with **email/password** accounts will be prompted to log in with Okta SSO.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Google SSO](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction)

# Kalshi - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Navigation

Kalshi

Kalshi

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Event Contracts](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#event-contracts)
    
*   [Key Features](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#key-features)
    
*   [Company History](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#company-history)
    
*   [Kalshi Data on Dune](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#kalshi-data-on-dune)
    

Kalshi is the first CFTC regulated exchange dedicated to trading on the outcome of future events. From inflation, to fed rates, to unemployment, to will the government shut down, Kalshi allows people to trade on a broad range of topics. Kalshi has developed a new asset class, event contracts, where you can buy Yes or No positions with respect to whether an event will happen or not. Kalshi’s vision is to allow people to capitalize on their opinions, trade in the domain of every day, and hedge risks that relate to them.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#event-contracts)

Event Contracts
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kalshi’s Event Contracts give people the ability to trade based on their opinions about a specific yes-or-no question. For example, if you have student debt and are worried about relief not passing, you can purchase a contract and get a payout even if it doesn’t pass. If you’re worried about the economic fallout of the government shutting down, you can place a trade to hedge against it. If you’ve developed a model on inflation, you can profit from that and maybe even offset your rising costs. Event Contracts have an interesting side effect - the price that a given event contract trades at is actually the market’s assessment of the probability that the event will happen. Kalshi’s inflation and federal rate forecasts have been more accurate than economists, pundits, and traditional news outlets over the past year. Kalshi offers Event Contracts on a wide range of topics, including economics, culture, weather, scientific advancements, and traditional financial markets such as commodities, forex, S&P, and NASDAQ indices.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#key-features)

Key Features
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **CFTC Regulated**: Kalshi is regulated by the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC) as a Designated Contract Market (DCM)
*   **Event-Based Trading**: Trade on the outcome of future events with Yes or No positions
*   **Broad Market Coverage**: Event contracts on economics, politics, sports, culture, crypto, climate, health, and more
*   **Market Probability Assessment**: Event contract prices reflect the market’s assessment of event probability
*   **Risk Hedging**: Ability to hedge against everyday risks and economic events
*   **Election Trading**: First fully regulated platform in over a century to offer legal election trading in the United States

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#company-history)

Company History
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kalshi was founded in 2018 by Tarek Mansour and Luana Lopes Lara, who met while studying at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology (MIT). During their early careers at financial institutions like Goldman Sachs, Citadel, and Bridgewater, Tarek and Luana observed that many financial decisions were driven by predictions about future events. However, they noticed a gap in the market: there was no straightforward way for people to trade directly on event outcomes. In 2019, Kalshi was accepted into Y Combinator’s Winter batch, where the team further developed the platform. In 2020, Kalshi made history by becoming the first fully regulated financial exchange in the U.S. specifically for event contracts, officially designated as a Designated Contract Market (DCM) by the CFTC. In 2024, Kalshi achieved a historic milestone by becoming the first fully regulated platform in over a century to offer legal election trading in the United States, following a federal appeals court ruling that upheld Kalshi’s right to list contracts on political outcomes.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/overview#kalshi-data-on-dune)

Kalshi Data on Dune
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Market Report\
-------------\
\

[Trade Report\
------------\
\
Contains trade execution data and transaction information](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/trade_report)

[Kalshi Website\
--------------\
\
Learn more about Kalshi, event contracts, and the platform](https://kalshi.com/about)

Initia

Initia Data

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/overview#what-is-initia)

What is Initia?
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Initia’s core philosophy is to make opinionated decisions on the underlying infrastructure such as data availability, interoperability, and oracles. By reducing decision fatigue, the Interwoven Stack empowers developers with the tools to craft application-specific environments while maintaining un-fragmented accessibility to the application ecosystem. Initia provides a framework that powers all of Initia’s rollups through the Interwoven Stack, featuring enshrined liquidity solutions for bootstrapping cross-chain liquidity while maintaining network security. The platform includes InitiaDEX, Minitswap, and a Vested Interest Program (VIP) that aims to foster long-term ecosystem-wide alignment.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/overview#key-features)

Key Features
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Interwoven Stack**: Framework that powers all of Initia’s rollups, enabling developers to craft application-specific environments
*   **Enshrined Liquidity**: Solution for bootstrapping cross-chain liquidity while maintaining network security
*   **VIP Program**: Incentive program that aims to foster long-term ecosystem-wide alignment
*   **InitiaDEX**: Decentralized exchange built on the Initia network
*   **Minitswap**: Swap functionality integrated into the ecosystem
*   **Developer-Friendly**: Tools and infrastructure that reduce decision fatigue for developers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/overview#initia-data-on-dune)

Initia Data on Dune
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Initia blockchain data is organized into several key tables that capture different aspects of on-chain activity:

[Balances\
--------\
\
Account balance snapshots and token holdings](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/balances)
[Blocks\
------\
\
Contains each validated block in the chain](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/blocks)
[Block Events\
------------\
\
Contains all block-level events and attributes in the chain, partitioned by event\_index](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/block_events)
[Bridge Transfers\
----------------\
\
Cross-chain bridge transfer data](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/bridge_transfers)
[Message Events\
--------------\
\
Contains all events and their corresponding attributes partitioned by message\_index](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/message_events)
[Swaps\
-----\
\
Token swap and liquidity pool data](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/swaps)
[Transactions\
------------\
\
Contains relevant data associated with each transaction](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/transactions)
[Transaction Messages\
--------------------\
\
Contains all messages submitted to the blockchain](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/tx_messages)
[Validators\
----------\
\
Maps validator addresses to monikers (human-readable description) and other metadata](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/initia/validators)

We’ve created tutorials covering all product surfaces of Dune—from navigating the platform and understanding data tables to creating compelling visualizations and becoming a skilled crypto data analyst.

New to Dune? Start with the [Getting Started](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#getting-started-with-dune)
 section and work your way through. Already familiar with the basics? Jump to the section that interests you most.

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#getting-started-with-dune)

Getting Started with Dune
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These videos will help you get up and running with Dune quickly, understanding how data flows through the platform and how to navigate the app effectively.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#dune-official-getting-started-series)

Dune Official Getting Started Series

Learn how the data flows and how to navigate the Dune app to create queries, visualizations, and dashboards. This comprehensive playlist covers all the essentials you need to get started.

[View the full playlist on YouTube →](https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLK3b5d4iK10ext4v-GBySekaA8-GP8quD)

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#creating-and-managing-dashboards)

Creating and Managing Dashboards
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Dashboards are where Dune’s content lives and gets discovered. Learn how to create dashboards, add widgets, embed visualizations, and share your work with the community.

**Related docs:** [Create Dashboards](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/dashboards)

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#learning-dunesql-and-our-engines)

Learning DuneSQL and Our Engines
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

DuneSQL is a Trino fork fine-tuned for blockchain analytics. Learn about its key features including varbinary data types, uint256 support, columnar storage, and materialized views.

**Related docs:** [Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#exploring-queries-views-and-matviews)

Exploring Queries (Views and Matviews)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Query Editor is where you’ll spend most of your time on Dune. Learn how to use its features effectively, including autocomplete, running query selections, and using keyboard shortcuts.

**Related docs:** [Writing Queries](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-window)

* * *

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#searching-and-contributing-to-spellbook)

Searching and Contributing to Spellbook
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Learn how to contribute to Dune’s curated datasets through Spellbook—our community-driven data modeling framework. Discover how curated datasets are built and learn how you can contribute your own data models to help the entire Dune community.

**Related docs:** [Curated Data](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/curated/overview)

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

More Tutorials

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#query-filters-vs-execution-parameters)

Query Filters vs Execution Parameters

Understand the two primary methods for fetching data from the Dune API: using filters with scheduled queries for speed, or executing queries with parameters for real-time data. This video explains when to use each approach.

**Related docs:** [Executions Overview](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object)
, [Filtering Results](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)

Building Farcaster Frames with Dune API

**Related docs:** [Build a Frame with Dune API](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/dune-frames)

# Query Editor Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Navigation

Write and Run Queries

Query Editor Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Left Sidebar](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#left-sidebar)
    
*   [Central Editor](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#central-editor)
    
*   [Right Sidebar](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#right-sidebar)
    
*   [Features at a Glance](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#features-at-a-glance)
    

The Query Editor is where you spend most of your time on Dune. It consists of three main areas:

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#left-sidebar)

Left Sidebar
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

The left sidebar gives you quick access to data discovery and query management tools. The most important panel here is the **[Data Explorer](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/data-explorer)
**, which connects you directly to Dune’s full [Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
 — letting you search for tables, inspect schemas, and insert columns into your query without leaving the editor.

*   **Data Explorer** — Browse and search across curated datasets, decoded contracts, raw blockchain tables, partner data, and your own uploaded data. You can search by table name, contract address, or keyword. See [Find Data Tables](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/data-explorer)
     for a full guide.
*   **Query Explorer** — Search for and locate existing queries relevant to your analysis.
*   **[Version History](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/version-history)
    ** — Review past edits to your query and revert to any previous version.
*   **Settings** — Configure query-level settings such as ownership and privacy.

Double-click any sidebar icon to collapse or expand it.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#central-editor)

Central Editor
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The central editor is your main workspace for writing and running SQL. It includes a full-featured code editor with autocomplete, syntax highlighting, and inline error messages, along with a results panel where you can view output, sort columns, and build visualizations. See [Writing Queries](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-window)
 for a detailed guide on editor features, autocomplete, keyboard shortcuts, and running queries.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#right-sidebar)

Right Sidebar
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The right sidebar contains tools for automating and exporting your work once a query is ready:

*   **[Query Scheduler](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler)
    ** — Set queries to run automatically on a recurring schedule so your dashboards and data stay up to date.
*   **[Materialized Views](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/materialized-views)
    ** — Save query results as reusable tables that other queries can reference directly.
*   **Export as CSV** — Download your query results for use in external tools or reports.
*   **[Alerts](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/alerts)
    ** — Configure notifications that trigger when your query results meet specific conditions.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor#features-at-a-glance)

Features at a Glance
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Writing Queries\
---------------\
\
Write and execute SQL using autocomplete, run selection, and keyboard shortcuts.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-window)
[Finding Tables\
--------------\
\
Browse and search Dune’s data catalog directly from the query editor sidebar.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/data-explorer)
[Parameters\
----------\
\
Add variables to your queries for dynamic, reusable analysis.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/parameters)
[Query Lineage\
-------------\
\
Visualize all tables, views, and nested query dependencies.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-lineage)
