# Schedule Queries and Dashboards - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Automate and Monitor

Schedule Queries and Dashboards

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [How to Schedule a Query](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#how-to-schedule-a-query)
    
*   [Query Scheduling Limitations](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#query-scheduling-limitations)
    
*   [Adjusting or Cancelling a Query Schedule](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#adjusting-or-cancelling-a-query-schedule)
    
*   [Scheduling entire dashboards](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#scheduling-entire-dashboards)
    

**Query Scheduling allows you to schedule a query to run at a specific time and frequency.** Queries on Dune usually execute when a user triggers an automatic or interactive execution. This means that if you have a dashboard that is not frequently viewed, the data displayed on the dashboard may be outdated and execution of the queries will only be triggered once a user views the dashboard. Especially for dashboards that contain resource-intensive queries, this can lead to long loading times for the viewer. To keep your dashboard up-to-date and to ensure that your queries are executed reliably and in a timely manner, you can schedule them to run at a specific time and frequency. Scheduled queries can be run on medium and large query engines, which will require credits. Credits are consumed based on actual compute resources used for each scheduled query execution.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#how-to-schedule-a-query)

How to Schedule a Query

1.  Start by clicking the scheduler (clock) icon located at the bottom of the query editor, to the left of the “Run” button
2.  A dialog will prompt you to set a refresh schedule and an execution tier. Please note that scheduled queries can only be run on medium and large query engines, which will require credits.
3.  The dialog will display an estimated monthly credit consumption for this query scheduling, along with a monthly quota. These values will adjust based on the frequency and execution tier you select.
4.  Save the schedule
5.  Your query will execute once to start the schedule, and then will execute according to the schedule you set.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#query-scheduling-limitations)

Query Scheduling Limitations

*   Query scheduling is currently not available for queries with parameters.
*   The query schedule is removed when the queries are archived or when the ownership changes (e.g., when a query is migrated).
*   There are no notifications available for scheduled query failures as of now. Rest assured, these failures do not result in any charges to your account.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#adjusting-or-cancelling-a-query-schedule)

Adjusting or Cancelling a Query Schedule

To modify or cancel a query schedule, click the scheduler (clock) icon again to reopen the scheduling dialog. From there you can adjust the frequency, time, or execution tier. To stop the schedule entirely, scroll to the bottom of the dialog and click the **Stop** button. ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/YGGGbX8CdbsnZ9Ri/web-app/query-editor/images/query-scheduler/cancel-scheduled-query.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=YGGGbX8CdbsnZ9Ri&q=85&s=57f439209388a8ce05babe5985e00138)

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/query-scheduler#scheduling-entire-dashboards)

Scheduling entire dashboards

Instead of scheduling individual queries, you can also schedule entire dashboards. Learn more about scheduling dashboards [here](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/dashboards#sharing-your-dashboard)
.

Visualize and Present Results

Charts and Graphs

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)

On this page

*   [Chart Types](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#chart-types)

*   [X/Y-axis Tick and Label formats](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#x%2Fy-axis-tick-and-label-formats)
    

Visualizations make your data come to life. You can create a visualization from any query result to surface trends, compare metrics, and share insights visually.

Watch our [visualization tutorial video](https://docs.dune.com/resources/learning/video-tutorials#creating-graphs--charts)
 to see how to create charts step-by-step.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#chart-types)

Chart Types
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Dune supports the following chart types. You can mix multiple types in a single visualization — for example, combining bars and lines — as long as your base chart is not a pie chart. Expand each type below to see an example.

Bar Charts

![bar chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/bar-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=f209ee6996a68b1bdc71af6478f11f66)

Area Charts

![area chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/area-chart.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=4786100cba4f970b4eb6e1671d0e6371)

Scatter Charts

![scatter chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/scatter-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=0d82ad0597560b3fceab58488a5debed)

Line Charts

![line chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/line-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=bcfc6e28e1dc0143e02f5922d02cc490)

Pie Charts

![pie chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/pie-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=04dcb76783d87935521583d923f58702)

Mixed Graphs

![mixed graph example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/mixed-graph-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=a2c4ff95a67d66268d0cd677d08c0c85)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#visualization-configuration-options)

Visualization Configuration Options
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All chart types share a common set of configuration options. Use the tabs below to learn how to customize each aspect of your visualization. ![all visualization configuration options](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/all-visualization-configuration-options.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=2a6dd2b6a60ce366ffbf635c8c033f8b)

*   Chart options
    
*   Result data
    
*   X-axis options
    
*   Y-axis options
    
*   Series options
    
*   Pie options
    

This section allows you to define how to display your data.![see explanations below](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-4.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=eeaf2da596b6bbb8a6380aab6bb1f877)**Title**

*   The title will appear in all instances of this graph prominently at the top.
*   The graph will always keep the name of the Query, even if you edit this.

**Show chart legend**

*   Ticking this box will enable or disable the legend for the chart.

**Enable stacking**

*   If applicable, ticking this box will stack the chart values on top of each other based on the x-axis values.
*   If this is not turned on, the values will be plotted individually on the y-axis.
*   The calculation underpinning this will always group the value corresponding to one value on the x-axis. Make sure your data is clean in able for this to work (avoid gaps in your data).

**Normalize to percentage data**

*   This will normalize the chart to display percentage values of the chosen data table.
*   The calculation underpinning this will always group the value corresponding to one value on the x-axis. Make sure your data is clean in able for this to work (avoid gaps in your data).

**Show data labels**

*   Ticking this box leads to the display of the individual datapoints inside of the graph.
*   This only makes sense in cases where you have few datapoints that are spread out far enough from each other to not overlap.

Here you can pick the data points that are to be displayed.![see explanations below](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-5.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=c3fc9d257717e14ddb9382e021f54155)You can choose one **x-axis** and multiple **y-axis.**Alternatively, you can also choose one data series on the y-axis and choose to group it by a different column of your table (as shown in the example above).

Using these options you can influence how your x-axis data gets displayed.![see explanations below](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-6.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=f9285168bdeff49212ffc9d22cb8f91b)**Axis title**

*   This field allows you to specify a title for your x-axis.

**Sort Values**

*   by ticking this box you can specify if you want the values in your chart to be ordered.
*   If your x-axis is a time series, this will automatically happen.

**Reverse value**

*   Ticking this box will reverse the order of the values on the x-axis.

**Logarithmic**

*   Ticking this box will make your x-axis values display \_\_ logarithmically.

With these options you can influence how your y-axis data gets displayed.![see explanations below](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-7.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=5f829a3b44698bb4f2f60897f8f6e17a)**Axis title**

*   This field allows you to specify a title for your y-axis.

**Logarithmic**

*   Ticking this box will make your y-axis values display logarithmically.

**Enable right y-axis**

*   Ticking this box will enable an additional y-axis that you can plot values on.
*   You can choose in the [chart series section](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#ordering-your-series)
     what you want to be displayed on the left and right axis.

![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-9.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=a83167f291e3d0b9855cbfdefd6e51ac)In this section of the Visualization editor you can finalize your graph.

*   You can rename the “series” by simply clicking into the field.
*   You can change the chart type by clicking into the dropdown.
*   You can change the colors by clicking into the color box.
*   Finally you can also change the order of the series.

**Picking Colors**You can pick colors with your browser native color selector.This might look slightly different for you depending on which browser you use.![Choose any color you want!](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-color.gif?s=53484f9452c7189790f0ddaaf726a75e)

![pie options](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/pie-options.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=cf958798caeb861d5bf36f604ac31ecf)**Label format**

*   This field allows you to define the [tick format](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#xy-axis-tick-and-label-formats)
     of the data labels in your pie chart.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#x/y-axis-tick-and-label-formats)

X/Y-axis Tick and Label formats

![image](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-8.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=43c573aa100324be68c21de4e34a61fc) Tick formats change how numeric values and axis labels in your graphs are displayed. Here’s how to format them:

| Starting Value | Tick/Label format | Output | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1256784.3745 | `[blank]` | 1256784.3745000 | Displays the number 7 decimal precision. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0` | 1256784 | Displays only the integer. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0,0` | 1,256,784 | Only displays the integer with comma separation. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0,0.00` | 1,256,784.38 | Displays the number with `[x]` decimal precision, where `[x]` is the number of `0` you add after the decimal point. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0.0a` | 1.2M | Displays the number with `[x]` precision and a letter based on the number’s `1e[y]` power (eg “m” for million, “b” for billion) |
| 1256784.3745 | `$0.0a` | $1.2M | Adds a ”$” to the number. Works with all formats above though use of the `a` suffix is recommended. Currently the only ”$” is the only supported currency symbol. |

Was this page helpful?

# Teams and Roles - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Manage Your Team

Teams and Roles

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Create a Team](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#create-a-team)
    
*   [Invite Members and Assign Roles](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#invite-members-and-assign-roles)
    
*   [Team Content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#team-content)
    
*   [Switch Between Contexts](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#switch-between-contexts)
    
*   [Manage Subscriptions](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#manage-subscriptions)
    
*   [Transfer Ownership](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#transfer-ownership)
    
*   [Transfer a Query](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#transfer-a-query)
    
*   [Transfer a Dashboard](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#transfer-a-dashboard)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#faq)
    

Team accounts on Dune provide a shared workspace for collaboration. Teams can be created without a paid plan, but [Plus and Enterprise subscription features](https://dune.com/pricing)
 are available only to teams, not individual accounts. **Key benefits:**

*   **Collaborate on shared content.** Multiple team members work on the same queries and dashboards.
*   **Shared credits and paid features.** All team members can spend credits and access private content.
*   **Team profile.** Showcase all of your team’s work in one place.
*   **Role-based access.** Assign viewers, editors, or admins to control permissions.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#create-a-team)

Create a Team
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Navigate to the **global context switcher** at the top of the page.
2.  Select **“Create new team”** from the dropdown.
3.  Complete the team creation process.

Every team must have a unique name that has not been used before.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#invite-members-and-assign-roles)

Invite Members and Assign Roles
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After creating your team, invite members and assign roles:

*   **Admin:** Full control over settings, memberships, and content.
*   **Editor:** Can create and edit queries and dashboards under the team.
*   **Viewer:** Can view team content and spend credits.

Click **“Invite People”** in the team settings or share a direct invitation URL.

When you invite a user, they receive an email with a link to join. They can also go to [Settings > Teams](https://dune.com/settings/teams)
 to accept the invite.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#team-content)

Team Content
---------------------------------------------------------------------

Team queries and dashboards are created the same way as individual content. The **context** you are in (personal or team) determines who owns the content you create. You can change ownership of any query or dashboard in its Settings page. ![Team content](https://mintcdn.com/dune/cGOHlF0puMR7caG6/web-app/images/teams/query-settings-new.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=cGOHlF0puMR7caG6&q=85&s=e7db800bc165b9aac00f737273250653)

Once you transfer content to a team, only an Admin can transfer it back out. If you accidentally transfer content, ask a team Admin to transfer it back.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#switch-between-contexts)

Switch Between Contexts
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the global context switcher to toggle between your personal account and team accounts. The context determines:

*   Which content appears in “My Creations”
*   Which credit balance is used for query execution
*   Who owns newly created content

![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/cGOHlF0puMR7caG6/web-app/images/teams/context-switcher-new.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=cGOHlF0puMR7caG6&q=85&s=a575247c1e47cac7838bf4b232ceedee) You can spend team credits on any content regardless of ownership, and edit team content from either context. Version History edits are always attributed to your personal account.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#manage-subscriptions)

Manage Subscriptions
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Navigate to the team account settings page to:

*   **Modify your plan:** Change subscription plan or switch to annual billing.
*   **View usage statistics:** Check credits, CSV uploads, and private content quotas. You can also [export detailed credit usage data](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/credit-system-on-dune#export-credit-usage-data)
    .
*   **Manage additional credits:** Set a maximum dollar amount for pay-as-you-go credits in the “Limit extra credits” field (default is $0).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#transfer-ownership)

Transfer Ownership
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can transfer ownership of queries and dashboards between team members, teams, or your personal account.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#transfer-a-query)

Transfer a Query

1.  Click the cogwheel button to open query settings.
2.  In the “Owner” dropdown, select the new owner — you can transfer to a team member or to a team.

![Transfer query ownership between a user and a team](https://mintcdn.com/dune/njsi6hUWS8fj_Gsl/web-app/images/teams/user-team-dune-data-hub-transfer.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=njsi6hUWS8fj_Gsl&q=85&s=333073f810277ff2c15861379cd5114c)

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#transfer-a-dashboard)

Transfer a Dashboard

1.  Click **Edit**, then **Settings** to open the modal.
2.  Select the new owner in the “Owner” dropdown.

You can view ownership changes in the [Version History](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/version-history)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#faq)

FAQ
---------------------------------------------------

Can I have private content?

Private dashboards and queries are available for the team or personal account they belong to.

How do I change my role?

Ask one of your team admins. Every team must always have at least one admin.

Can I remove people from my team?

Yes, in the People section of your team’s Settings page.

Can I transfer content to another team?

Yes, in the Settings page of the query or dashboard you want to transfer.

Can I transfer content to another user?

Yes, but the target user must be a member of your team. If they are not, invite them first.

Can I transfer content to my personal account?

Yes, in the Settings page of the query or dashboard you want to transfer.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[FAQs](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/faqs)
[Google SSO](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/google-sso-domain-restriction)

Jump start your Dune journey with our collection of pre-built query templates. These templates let you easily select wallets, tokens, and contracts and track their key actions over time.

**Need a specific template?** Don’t see what you’re looking for? [Request a new template](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSeDjR0908lRRroCzRHSD9SnBKSS5hox-_AbLJahH7ZmBuf5hA/viewform?usp=header)
 and we’ll consider adding it to our collection.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#tokens)

Tokens
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Track token flows, balances, and holder activity across different token standards.

Contract Balance and Flow Monitoring - ERC20 Token

Track the net flows of an ERC20 token into contracts, over a given time period.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5823843)

Wallet Balance and Flow Monitoring - ERC20 Token

Track the net flows of top holders (or a list of addresses) for an ERC20 token, over a given time period.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5823857)

Contract Balance and Flow Monitoring - NFT Token (721/1155)

Track the net flows of an NFT token into contracts, over a given time period.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5823861)

Wallet Balance and Flow Monitoring - NFT Token (721/1155)

Track the net flows of top holders (or a list of addresses) for an NFT token, over a given time period.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833534)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#trades)

Trades
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Monitor trading activity across DEXs and NFT marketplaces.

DEX Trade Monitoring

Track trading volume, price movements, and liquidity patterns for token pairs.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833536)

NFT Trade Monitoring

Monitor NFT trading activity, floor prices, and collection performance.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833538)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#contracts)

Contracts
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Analyze smart contract interactions and usage patterns.

New Wallets Calling a Contract

Identify new users interacting with a specific smart contract over time.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833540)

New Contracts Calling Another Contract

Track which new contracts are calling a specific contract.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833541)

Trending Contracts Called by Tracked Wallet

Discover which contracts a tracked wallet is calling most frequently.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833544)

Farcaster
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Analyze social activity and user behavior on the Farcaster protocol.

Identify trending users who hold a token

Find Farcaster users who hold specific tokens and are gaining social traction.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833549)

Identify trending channels

Discover which Farcaster channels are gaining popularity and activity.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833553)

Track trending users someone has interacted with

Analyze the social network of a specific user to find trending connections.

[Open in Dune →](https://dune.com/queries/5833555)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#how-to-use-templates)

How to Use Templates
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Expand any template** above to see a preview of the query results
2.  **Click “Open in Dune”** to open the query in the Dune editor
3.  **Customize the parameters** using the template’s input fields:
    *   **Token Symbol**: Choose the token you want to track
    *   **Token Contract**: Paste the contract address if the token isn’t in our database
    *   **Blockchain**: Select the blockchain network
    *   **Time Period**: Set the number of days to analyze
    *   **Filters**: Adjust minimum thresholds and other parameters
4.  **Run the query** to see your results
5.  **Save and share** your customized query

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#template-categories-explained)

Template Categories Explained
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#tokens-2)

**Tokens**

Perfect for analyzing token economics, holder behavior, and token flows. Use these templates to understand how tokens move between wallets and contracts.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#trades-2)

**Trades**

Ideal for market analysis, price tracking, and trading pattern identification. Essential for understanding market dynamics and liquidity.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#contracts-2)

**Contracts**

Great for smart contract analytics, user adoption tracking, and protocol interaction analysis. Use these to understand how users interact with specific protocols.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#farcaster-2)

**Farcaster**

Designed for social analytics on the Farcaster protocol. Perfect for understanding community dynamics, influencer identification, and social trends.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#getting-started)

Getting Started
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Choose your category** based on what you want to analyze
2.  **Select a template** that matches your use case
3.  **Customize the parameters** to fit your specific needs
4.  **Run and iterate** to refine your analysis

**Pro Tip**: Start with a template and modify it to create your own unique queries. Templates are designed to be building blocks for more complex analysis.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/query-templates#need-help)

Need Help?
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Query Editor Guide**: Learn how to use the Dune query editor effectively
*   **Writing Efficient Queries**: Optimize your queries for better performance
*   **Data Catalog**: Explore available data sources and tables
*   **Community**: Join our Discord for help and inspiration

* * *

**Don’t see what you need?** [Request a new template](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSeDjR0908lRRroCzRHSD9SnBKSS5hox-_AbLJahH7ZmBuf5hA/viewform?usp=header)
 and we’ll consider adding it to our collection.

# Create your first visualization - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-visualization#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Navigation

Visualize and Present Results

Create your first visualization

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

After executing a query, you’ll be presented with a set of results. The next logical step? Visualize that data for a clearer insight. This guide will show you how to layer a combined bar and line chart atop the data from [Create your first query](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query)
. Here is a visual click-through version if you are more of a visual learner. Below is a written version.

1.  **Begin Visualization**: Click on “New” and select your desired chart type. For this tutorial, initiate with a bar chart and click “Bar Chart.”
2.  **Display Data**: By default, the chart will showcase `monthly_gas_spent`. To augment the depth of insights, include the `cumulative_gas_spent` column.
3.  **Adjust Chart Type**: Transition the representation of `cumulative_gas_spent` from a bar to a line chart, offering a more nuanced view.
4.  **Fine-tune Your Chart**: Customize the display values for a polished look. For detailed formatting guidance, [refer to this resource](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs)
    .

You can also use the AI Chart Builder to automatically generate the charts for your data.

1.  **Click Generate** When you click generate, the AI Chart Builder will suggest a title and chart type based on your data.
2.  If you are happy with the recommendation, click **Create** to add the chart to your dashboard.
3.  Otherwise, you can edit the title or the chart type and then click **Create** to create the chart.
4.  (Optional) **Fine-tune Your Chart**: Customize the display values for a polished look. For detailed formatting guidance, [refer to this resource](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs)
    .

# Create your first query - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Write and Run Queries

Create your first query

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)

On this page

*   [Getting Started](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#getting-started)
    
*   [Choosing the Right Table](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#choosing-the-right-table)
    
*   [Building Your Query Step by Step](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#building-your-query-step-by-step)
    
*   [Understanding the Query Components](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#understanding-the-query-components)
    
*   [Making Your Analysis Dynamic with Parameters](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#making-your-analysis-dynamic-with-parameters)
    
*   [Visualizing Results](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#visualizing-results)
    
*   [Next Steps](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#next-steps)
    

New to Dune? Let’s start your analytics journey by creating an insightful query that analyzes daily DEX trading volumes across different blockchains. This guide will teach you the basics while delivering practical insights about DeFi trading activity.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#getting-started)

Getting Started
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Create a New Query**: Head over to [Create New Query](https://dune.com/queries)
 to begin. Dune uses DuneSQL, a SQL dialect that is compatible with TrinoSQL. It is a fairly vanilla SQL dialect, but there are some nuances you will eventually encounter. If you are not familiar with SQL, you can learn the basics [here](https://www.w3schools.com/sql/)
.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#choosing-the-right-table)

Choosing the Right Table
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Choosing the right table is the first step to creating a successful query. You can find the table you need in the [Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog)
.

1.  **Understanding curated data**: Instead of working with complex raw blockchain data, we’ll use Dune’s curated data - a collection of pre-built, analytics-ready tables. Curated data standardizes data across chains and makes analysis much easier.
2.  **The Perfect Table**: For DEX trading analysis, we’ll use the [`dex.trades`](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/data-catalog/curated/dex-trades/evm/dex-trades)
     table. This table contains standardized trading data across multiple DEXes and blockchains.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#building-your-query-step-by-step)

Building Your Query Step by Step
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Let’s analyze DEX trading activity across different blockchains. We’ll start simple and build up our analysis:

1.  **Select Key Metrics**: For our DEX analysis, we’ll track:
    *   Block date (to see trends over time)
    *   Blockchain (to compare activity across networks)
    *   Trading volume in USD
    *   Number of trades

Here’s our query:

Copy

Ask AI

    SELECT
      block_date,
      blockchain,
      COUNT(*) as number_of_trades,
      SUM(amount_usd) as trading_volume_usd
    FROM dex.trades
    WHERE
      block_date >= NOW() - INTERVAL '30' day
    GROUP BY
      1, 2
    ORDER BY
      1 DESC, 4 DESC
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#understanding-the-query-components)

Understanding the Query Components
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each part of this query helps us analyze DEX activity:

*   `block_date`: Groups all trades into daily buckets
*   `blockchain`: Helps us compare activity across Ethereum, Polygon, Arbitrum, etc.
*   `COUNT(*)`: Gives us the trading frequency
*   `SUM(amount_usd)`: Shows the total value traded in USD
*   `WHERE block_date >= NOW() - INTERVAL '30 days'`: Focuses on recent activity
*   `GROUP BY 1, 2, 3`: Combines trades by day, blockchain, and DEX
*   `ORDER BY 1 DESC, 5 DESC`: Shows newest and highest volume trades first

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#making-your-analysis-dynamic-with-parameters)

Making Your Analysis Dynamic with Parameters
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Want to focus on your favorite DEX? Let’s add the column `project` as a parameter to make the analysis interactive:

Copy

Ask AI

    SELECT
      block_date,
      blockchain,
      project,
      COUNT(*) as number_of_trades,
      SUM(amount_usd) as trading_volume_usd
    FROM dex.trades
    WHERE
      block_date >= NOW() - INTERVAL '30' day
      AND project = '{{Project Name}}' -- Try 'uniswap' or 'curve'
    GROUP BY
      1, 2, 3
    ORDER BY
      1 DESC, 5 DESC
    

To add the parameter:

1.  Click “Add Parameter” below the query editor
2.  Create a text parameter named “Project Name”
3.  Set default value to “Uniswap”

Now you can instantly switch between different DEXes to compare their performance!

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#visualizing-results)

Visualizing Results
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After running your query, you can create powerful visualizations:

1.  Click “New Visualization”
2.  Choose “Bar Chart”
3.  Set X-axis to `trading_day`
4.  Set Y-axis to `trading_volume_usd`
5.  Group by `blockchain`

This will create a stacked bar chart showing daily trading volumes by blockchain!

Want to explore more? Try:

*   Removing the project filter to see all DEXes
*   Changing the time period to 7 days or 90 days
*   Adding token filters to focus on specific cryptocurrencies

[​](https://docs.dune.com/learning/how-tos/create-your-first-query#next-steps)

Next Steps
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Congratulations on creating your first DEX analysis query! 🎉 You can find many more queries related to DEX trading activity in this dashboard: [DEX Trading Activity](https://dune.com/hagaetc/dex-metrics)
 Save your query by clicking **Save** in the upper right corner. You can revisit and modify it anytime to explore different aspects of DEX trading activity.

Ready to create more advanced queries? Check out our other guides to learn more about Dune

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

# How Contract Decoding Works - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#content-area)

Decode Smart Contracts

How Contract Decoding Works

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [A. The Lifecycle of Decoding](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#a-the-lifecycle-of-decoding)
    
*   [Step 1: Submission](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#step-1-submission)
    
*   [When do you need Several Instances Options?](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#when-do-you-need-several-instances-options)

*   [Decode other contracts created by the same factory](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#decode-other-contracts-created-by-the-same-factory)
    
*   [Dynamic vs Factory Decoded](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#dynamic-vs-factory-decoded)
    
*   [Other Special Contracts](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#other-special-contracts)
    
*   [Proxy contract](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#proxy-contract)

*   [Additional Questions?](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#additional-questions)
    

**Dune’s extensive catalog of decoded smart contracts are driven by our analysts. Our decoding process empowers our community to submit the data and build the tables that they’d like to query on Dune!** But what does decoding mean? Blockchain transaction data starts as bytecode, a low level programming language that can be read by machines. Using the ABI (Application Binary Interface) that is specific to each contract, we translate that bytecode into query-able data tables.

[Explore decoded data\
--------------------](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/ethereum/decoded/overview)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#a-the-lifecycle-of-decoding)

A. The Lifecycle of Decoding
==========================================================================================================================

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#step-1-submission)

Step 1: Submission
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Our decoding process begins with our [contract submission page](https://dune.com/contracts/new)
. ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/SVgi72CZX0mBmKw8/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/submit-contract-03202025.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=SVgi72CZX0mBmKw8&q=85&s=8cc926ce172af60d644a464cc115e49f) To successfully submit a contract, you will need four pieces of information:

1.  **Blockchain**: Blockchain the contract is deployed on
2.  **Contract Address**: The address of the contract you want to decode
3.  **Project Name**: The name of the project that the contract originates from (e.g. Tether, Uniswap, Bancor)
4.  **Contract Name**: The name of the smart contract as given by the project (ex. USDT, Pair, LiquidityFactory)
5.  **ABI**: Unique to each smart contract. Further details can be found [here](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/latest/abi-spec.html)
    . Note that for contracts that are verified by a chain’s explorer we will attempt to auto-fetch the ABI. Otherwise the ABI will need to be entered manually.

In most cases, the contract name will be pulled directly from a blockchain scanner. We recommend using the name provided. If the name is not automatically provided, please follow our naming conventions to assure the contract is properly assimilated into Dune’s database.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#when-do-you-need-several-instances-options)

When do you need Several Instances Options?

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#enable-bytecode-matching)

Enable bytecode matching

Contract “instances” are contracts on the same chain with the same bytecode (and therefore the same ABI) for **the same project**. If you check this box, Dune can decode all instances of this project on the given blockchain with the same bytecode and ABI, consolidating them into the same tables under one `namespace.project` directory without multiple submissions. To check for other instances of the contract, go to a blockchain explorer and look for “Similar Match Source Code” under the Contract tab. Here is [an example](https://etherscan.io/address/0x58a70c59cb1f0e30c3d7ad84b96170221cbf322f#code)
: ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/similar-match-source-code.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=734521f8b4531115b879f4a8b2349fcd) **Decoded via dynamic contract detection** Contracts decoded this way are referred to as dynamically decoded by Dune. These are contracts that are decoded automatically because users checked the box “Are there several instances of this contract?” when submitting the contract. Note that Dune only considers a contract a dynamic instance if the bytecode matches 100%. This is done by querying the `<chain>_creation_traces` table and matching the `code` field. If the bytecode does not match 100%, we will not decode that instance. For example, [this contract](https://arbiscan.io/address/0x999946a4f40fd2c82d66a68edfefa8430f206c9c#code)
 is nearly identical to [this other contract](https://arbiscan.io/address/0x692e92da68f9b8445a167b985ee0cb38c3bbe594#code)
 in terms of bytecode, but Dune currently does not dynamically decode the first contract because we currently require a 100% bytecode match.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#decode-other-contracts-created-by-the-same-factory)

Decode other contracts created by the same factory

A [factory contract](https://betterprogramming.pub/learn-solidity-the-factory-pattern-75d11c3e7d29)
 is a smart contract that creates other smart contracts. If there are multiple instances of a contract, it might be due to a factory contract. If you check this box, Dune can decode all contracts created by the same factory that use the same ABI, consolidating them into the same tables under one `namespace.project` directory (e.g., [Pair contract from Uniswap V2](https://dune.com/queries?category=decoded_project&blockchain=ethereum&namespace=uniswap_v2&contract=Pair&blockchains=ethereum)
). When you submit a contract as a factory contract, Dune verifies it by checking if the deployer (`from` address) is a contract and not an EOA. This is done by querying the `<chain>_creation_traces` table. If the `from` address is a contract, Dune will gather all `address` fields created by it for decoding. To check if a contract is created by a factory, use a blockchain explorer to see if the “From” address in a Contract Creation transaction is a contract or an EOA. For example, this is [a factory-created contract](https://etherscan.io/address/0x5d5ce36e0b328a48539b48d4f22c31f0fe3dc040#internaltx)
 by [Uniswap V3 factory](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1f98431c8ad98523631ae4a59f267346ea31f984)
. ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/factory-created-contract.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=1d4a141247b9a9cede439f42945cc4eb) **Decoded via the factory pattern** Contracts decoded this way are referred to as factory decoded by Dune. These contracts are automatically decoded because users checked “Is it created by a factory contract?” when submitting. Dune detects this by querying the `<chain>_creation_traces` table and fetching all `address` fields created by the same `from`.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#dynamic-vs-factory-decoded)

Dynamic vs Factory Decoded

Dynamic decoding anchors on the bytecode being the same, while factory decoding also requires the contract to be deployed by another contract (not an EOA) with the same deployer address. **Dynamically Decoded Contracts** share the same bytecode but may have different deployers. For example, [this contract](https://etherscan.io/address/0x58a70c59cb1f0e30c3d7ad84b96170221cbf322f)
 can be decoded as dynamic because it has the same bytecode as [this contract](https://etherscan.io/address/0x6d396aaff9f438e2f86979d8367cd9deb364b16f)
. Both will appear under the same decoded tables in the [SmartTokens for Bancor](https://dune.com/queries?category=decoded_project&blockchain=ethereum&namespace=bancor&contract=SmartToken&blockchains=ethereum)
 directory but have different deployers (`from` address). **Factory Decoded Contracts** are deployed by a factory contract and share the same deployer address. For example, contracts created by the [Uniswap V3 Factory](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1f98431c8ad98523631ae4a59f267346ea31f984)
, such as [this one](https://etherscan.io/address/0xb5925e4c1912e3999891f0e71bd3d9b5492d1486#internaltx)
 and [this one](https://etherscan.io/address/0x5d5ce36e0b328a48539b48d4f22c31f0fe3dc040#internaltx)
, are factory decoded because they share the same bytecode and deployer. These contracts will appear under the same decoded tables in the [Pair for Uniswap V3](https://dune.com/queries?category=decoded_project&blockchain=ethereum&namespace=uniswap_v3&contract=Pair&blockchains=ethereum)
 directory.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#other-special-contracts)

Other Special Contracts

Other special smart contracts can be decoded as well, following these conventions:

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#proxy-contract)

[Proxy contract](https://info.etherscan.com/what-is-proxy-contract/)

Submit using the proxy address but with the ABI of the implementation. You can identify a proxy contract by looking for the “Read as Proxy” tab on a blockchain explorer. This tab will also show the implementation contract. Here is [an example](https://arbiscan.io/address/0x90a664846960aafa2c164605aebb8e9ac338f9a0#readProxyContract)
. ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/proxy-find-implementation.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=d0e12e9d30802b33b1e20a96a7f5fc04) To decode:

1.  Use the address of the [proxy contract](https://arbiscan.io/address/0x90a664846960aafa2c164605aebb8e9ac338f9a0)
    .
2.  Fetch the ABI of the [implementation contract](https://arbiscan.io/address/0x90a664846960aafa2c164605aebb8e9ac338f9a0#readProxyContract)
    .

![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/submit-proxy-03202025.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=58ed24ece6a156c3ad81d2fb4c6c9edb)

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#diamond-proxy-contracts)

Diamond proxy contracts

Submit all the facets using just the same name for the project and contract and upload all the relevant ABIs. This can be done with one ABI representing all facets or separate ABIs for each facet.

**Where can I find this information?**Contract addresses can usually be found in a project’s docs. Once you have the contract address, you can use a blockchain explorer to get the rest of the information. Most blockchain explorers have everything you need!

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#resubmissions)

Resubmissions

Sometimes you need to resubmit a contract because the name is originally submitted wrong, or you need to update the ABI. Follow the steps as guided. But if you are resubmitting for other reason not listed in the dropdown, provide as much detail as possible to avoid the resubmission being rejected. ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/resubmission-contract.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=c961b8aa843f4e09d00ab3e439c54e5f)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#step-2-decoding)

Step 2: Decoding
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once the contract has been approved for decoding, you will receive a notification in your email. While the table itself may be visible after approval, it may be empty. No reason to worry! Note that it takes around 24 hours from the time the contract has been approved to be fully decoded and incorporated into the Dune database. At any point you can check the status of your submitted contract under “Contracts” in your settings.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#step-3-finding-your-decoded-contract)

Step 3: Finding Your Decoded Contract
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

One quick tip to find and begin querying your decoded table is to use Dune’s Explorer. When beginning a new query, the Explorer is located to the left side of the Query Editor. From there, follow simple steps:

1.  Drop the contract address of your decoded contract in the search bar
2.  Pull up the specific function or event you are looking for
3.  use the **\>>** button to immediately populate that table in your Query Editor.

![The search bar and >> symbol that will help you get started](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/decoding-contracts/3.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=cd9439402709f30520cdd0a73cbbd1b9) Then it’s all ready for you to query. Let the data flow!

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#b-need-help)

B. Need Help?
===========================================================================================

For frequently asked questions about decoding contracts, check out our [Decoding FAQs](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/faqs)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/decoding/decoding-contracts#additional-questions)

Additional Questions?

Head over to the [#decoding Discord channel](https://discord.com/channels/757637422384283659/850326962152538122)
 and we’ll be happy to help!

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#how-you-spend-credits-on-dune)

How you spend credits on Dune
====================================================================================================================================

Dune uses a usage-based credit system that charges based on actual compute resources consumed, ensuring fair pricing for all users regardless of query complexity. See full blog post announcement [here](https://dune.com/blog/credits-changing)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#how-the-credit-system-works)

How the Credit System Works
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Our query engine uses a flexible credit-based pricing model that scales with your actual resource consumption. When you run a query, credits are spent in proportion to the resources used—simple queries cost fewer credits, while complex queries that require more computational resources use more credits. This approach ensures fair pricing across our platform, which spans 100+ chains, complex tables, and multiple ways to consume data through APIs and various connector options. The credit system adapts to your needs: small, efficient queries are economical, while larger, more complex queries can leverage extended timeouts and additional resources as needed. Your credits work seamlessly across all query types and data consumption methods, providing transparent and predictable pricing that scales with your usage. **Key benefits:**

*   **Usage-based** – Pay in proportion to actual consumption
*   **Efficiency** – Incentives to write cleaner, optimized queries
*   **Scalable** – Sustainable future support for larger workloads with longer timeouts and expanded connector options to come in the near future

This fair, usage-based model ensures Dune can keep pace with your most ambitious data needs.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#credit-pricing)

Credit Pricing
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Credits are consumed based on the actual compute resources used for each query execution. The more complex your query, the more credits it consumes, but simple queries cost significantly less. At the moment, we don’t share a single, per-query formula because credit usage depends on real-time factors (the compute your query actually uses, the engine you choose, and current network/data access conditions. To stay in full control, you can set:

*   a global query cost cap (per-execution ceiling). More info on how to do this [here](https://app.arcade.software/share/C60r4u7ESOp5RXRuzbSN)
    .
*   a monthly extra credit limit (account-level ceiling). These controls ensure you never exceed what you’re comfortable spending per run or per month. Learn how to set this up [here](https://app.arcade.software/share/so8QGM4H4MU0OWRWhNe9)
    .

**Credit Pricing = Extra Credit Pricing**  
Extra credits are charged at the same rate as your plan. The price per 100 credits shown for each plan is what you pay for any usage beyond your included credits, keeping things simple and transparent. **Quick Plan Reference**

| Plan | Monthly Price | Annual Price | Credits/Month | Cost per 100 Credits |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Free** | Free | \-  | 2,500 | $5.00 |
| **Analyst** | $75/month | \-  | 4,000 | $1.875 |
| **Analyst (Annual)** | $65/month billed annually | $780/year | 4,000 | $1.625 |
| **Plus** | $399/month | \-  | 25,000 | $1.596 |
| **Plus (Annual)** | $349/month billed annually | $4,188/year | 25,000 | $1.396 |
| **Legacy Premium** | No longer available | \-  | Varies | [Contact support](mailto:support@dune.com) |
| **Enterprise** | Favorable Custom Pricing | \-  | Custom | **Favorable rates** - [Contact sales](https://dune.com/enterprise) |

**Save with Enterprise Pricing**: Enterprise plans receive **significantly lower per-credit rates** compared to standard plans, plus customized support and tailored solutions. Whether you’re scaling up or just getting started, [contact our sales team](https://dune.com/enterprise)
 to discuss custom pricing that fits your needs.

**Legacy Premium**: This plan is no longer available for new subscriptions. Existing Premium customers can continue to use their plan.

Explore the complete pricing plan with credit limits and features for each tier: [dune.com/pricing](https://dune.com/pricing)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#managing-your-credit-usage)

Managing Your Credit Usage
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Review your usage.** Check your query volume and costs regularly to stay informed about your credit consumption.
*   **Optimize your queries.** Efficient queries save credits and run faster. See [here](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/writing-efficient-queries)
     for tips.
*   **Pick the plan that fits.** If you anticipate heavy usage or notice extra credits usage, consider upgrading to Enterprise for **significantly lower per-credit rates**. Contact our sales team at [dune.com/enterprise](http://dune.com/enterprise)
     to discuss custom pricing and tailored solutions for your needs.
*   **Cap your query costs.** Control spending by setting a maximum credit limit for individual queries. More info on how to do this [here](https://app.arcade.software/share/C60r4u7ESOp5RXRuzbSN)
    .
*   **Set extra credit limits.** Configure your extra credit spending limits to control costs. Learn how to set this up [here](https://app.arcade.software/share/so8QGM4H4MU0OWRWhNe9)
    .

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#need-help)

Need Help?
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Have questions or need additional support? [Contact Us](mailto:support@dune.com)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#faq)

FAQ
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#pricing-&-plans)

Pricing & Plans

How does Dune's credit system work?

Dune uses a usage-based credit system that charges based on actual compute resources consumed. This ensures fair pricing where lightweight queries cost less and complex queries cost more based on their actual resource requirements, providing everyone with a fair and flexible experience.

Is there a Free plan?

Yes. The Free plan includes **2,500 credits per month at no cost**. With the usage-based system, credits are consumed based on actual query resources. Small, efficient queries use fewer credits, allowing you to run more queries within your monthly allowance. Larger or more complex queries will use credits more quickly. If you consistently need more capacity, you can upgrade to a paid plan anytime.

Can I run bigger queries if I stay on a Free plan?

Yes, but you will be limited to the Small and Medium engine. If you often hit timeout limits, consider the Analyst or Plus plans.

How are credits calculated?

Credits are based on the actual compute effort measured in CPU-seconds and network resources a query consumes. This means lightweight queries cost fewer credits, while complex, resource-intensive operations require more credits.At the moment, we don’t share a single, per-query formula because credit usage depends on real-time factors (the compute your query actually uses, the engine you choose, and current network/data access conditions).In practice: Credits scale with compute used. Heavier queries consume more credits; lighter ones consume fewer. Engine matters. Large runs complex queries fastest and therefore consumes credits at a higher rate than Medium; Small prioritizes queue time over speed and is most efficient for simple jobs.To stay in full control, you can set: a global query cost cap (per-execution ceiling), and a monthly extra credit limit (account-level ceiling).

I run a lot of API queries. Will they cost more?

Cost will depend on compute used by those API queries. You can check the usage dashboard in Settings to track API-specific consumption.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#usage-&-monitoring)

Usage & Monitoring

How can I monitor my credit consumption?

The usage and billing dashboard shows credits used, extra credits, and historical usage.

Will I see the cost before running a query?

You’ll see costs after execution.

Can I run bigger queries now?

Yes more complex queries and higher data volumes with longer timeouts for Enterprise clients.

What is a system user? Is that for scheduled jobs?

Yes, the system user represents automated executions on the Dune platform. This includes scheduled query runs, materialized view refreshes, and other background jobs that run without direct user interaction. When you see credit usage attributed to a system user, it typically means those credits were consumed by your scheduled queries or automated data refresh processes rather than manual query executions.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/how-credits-work#optimization-&-support)

Optimization & Support

How can I lower my credit usage?

Write efficient SQL, limit unnecessary joins or scans, and reuse results when possible. Our docs include [query optimization tips](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/writing-efficient-queries)
.

What if I consistently exceed my plan credits?

You can upgrade to a higher plan or contact our sales team to discuss a custom Enterprise solution.

Who do I contact for help?

Reach out to [support@dune.com](mailto:support@dune.com)
 or your Dune account manager for Enterprise plans.

Web3 Data Resources
===================================================================================================

After you’ve gone through the quickstart guide, you’ll be ready to start learning how to navigate the Web3 data analytics space. Analyzing protocols in web3 is both really easy and hard. It’s really easy because everything is transparent and standardized - a deployed contract has a set of functions and events that are pretty much immutable. However, it’s an ever-expanding data arena as new protocols, tokens, and wallets join the fray. To build your reputation as an expert analyst, you must stay centered on what you want to analyze and what metrics you want to present.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/web3-data-resources#dune-tutorials)

Dune Tutorials
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/web3-data-resources#metrics-driven-analysis)

Metrics-Driven Analysis

**Video Series:** Delve deep with our end-to-end video series guides:

*   [Uniswap in 12 Days](https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLK3b5d4iK10cIrN8c_au9RrC0_eBCOyR2)
     (includes metrics like price impact, TVL, MEV volume, liquidity stability)
*   [Gnosis Safe Point-in-Time](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=S-cctFmR828)
     (includes metrics like signers, diversification, and valuations)

**Dashboards for Insights:**

*   To understand token trends and contexts, check out ERC20 and NFT dashboards
*   To understand wallet/user segments, you’ll need to leverage labels to enhance your analysis

Once you have metrics and also understand the underlying tokens and users, it will start to become clear what that real narrative is. Try and pull together a few insights, and then create a compelling dashboard and story around them.

Don’t try too hard to capture everything at once - it will become overwhelming for both you and those you share it with.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/web3-data-resources#analysis-tips)

Analysis Tips
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Start with a solid foundation.** Master basic SQL and blockchain concepts.
*   **Scope Your Work:** When looking into a protocol, you’ll need to understand the contract architecture and context. That starts with functions, events, and wallet overviews.

Remember that no protocol lives in isolation - there is always some mix of onchain events happening. That could be some new airdrop, a new upstream/downstream protocol integration, large whales making moves, governance changes in protocol parameters, and more. Once you have a solid understanding of protocol history in usage, user, and integration trends, you’re ready to start building some metrics.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/resources/web3-data-resources#engage-with-the-community)

Engage with the Community
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When you’re done, be sure to share your work in the Discord `#📺︱show-your-work` channel and on Twitter tagging [@dune](https://twitter.com/dune)
. We’ll be sure to give great analysts a boost! Web3 is all about connecting with communities - your queries and dashboards will do nothing if you don’t share it around.

How Activity is Measured
=====================================================================================================

![Activity heatmap showing user contributions over time](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/images/activity-heatmap.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=96f38cf446bf2ce133426429892674a7) Activity on Dune is measured by combining different types of contributions:

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/user-activity#query-activity)

Query Activity

*   Creating new queries (including temp queries)
*   Updating existing queries
*   Deleting queries

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/user-activity#dashboard-activity)

Dashboard Activity

*   Creating new dashboards

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/user-activity#contract-activity)

Contract Activity

*   Submitting new contracts

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/user-activity#contributions-calculation)

Contributions Calculation
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each action counts as one contribution for that day. For example, if you:

*   Create 2 queries
*   Update 1 query
*   Create 1 dashboard
*   Submit 1 contract

Your total activity for that day would be 5 contribution. The activity heatmap shows your daily activity over time, helping you track your contributions to the Dune ecosystem.

# kalshi.market_report - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/market_report#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=6fec71d5070d0923eb2924321131b1c2)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=zh-3B8LgVmyrKOaG&q=85&s=2501750983cc95aa72d40acc6f005bd9)](https://docs.dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Kalshi

kalshi.market\_report

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Table Schema](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/market_report#table-schema)
    

The `kalshi.market_report` table contains market data and information about event contracts on Kalshi. Each row represents market statistics and metrics for a specific event contract ticker.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/kalshi/market_report#table-schema)

Table Schema
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

| Column Name | Data Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| block\_volume | double | Trading volume for the block period |
| category | string | Category of the event contract (e.g., Politics, Economics, Sports, etc.) |
| daily\_volume | double | Total trading volume for the day |
| date | string | Date of the market report |
| high | double | Highest price reached during the reporting period |
| low | double | Lowest price reached during the reporting period |
| open\_interest | double | Total number of outstanding contracts |
| payout\_type | string | Type of payout for the event contract |
| report\_ticker | string | Unique ticker identifier for the market report |
| status | string | Current status of the event contract market |
| ticker\_name | string | Name or description of the event contract ticker |
| \_updated\_at | timestamp | Last update timestamp |
| \_ingested\_at | timestamp | Ingestion timestamp |
